=== Tuesday April 27, 2004 ===

This week will not be over till next Monday morning comes

It's been asked recently what it is I'm on pager for.  While crack dealer does have it's allure.  Not to mention the latteral move options;  Pimp, Car thief, some combination of the three... I actually work in the Technology industry.  Much to the chagrin of my ever conflicted inner self.  I'm not a Doctor (though I hope to be a psychologist someday), and I'm not any other pager-related job.  Just technological support to people who just have nothing better to do at 2:30 in the morning than call me with an issue that resolves itself within 5 minutes.  If only they would have waited 5 minutes.

You all know my passions.  Writing, photography, art, anything at all creative.  I like helping people too.  Unfortunately, the kind of helping people I had envisioned for my future did not involve software, hardware, and everything in between the two.  Needless to say, there is some satisfaction in the problem solving involved in the work I do now.  It also helps me maintain the balance I usualy crave between the right and left side of my brain.  Crativity vs. Logic.  Passion vs. Reason.

And that's why I think I'll make a decent psychologist.  I have that internal conflict.  In truth, I think we all have conflict within of some sort or another.  I'm not going to pretend to anyone that I don't have conflict.  That I'm without issues.  That I'm above anyone.  I think the best approach to helping people is to show them that you know what they mean because you've been there before.  That they're not alone in their "crazy" thoughts or pasts.  Who knows.  I could be full of it right now.  Way out in left field and totaly wrong.  But I haven't gone through the training to be a psychologist beyond the first two years of University.  One thing I don't want is to become callous to people's problems.  I know it'll hurt to feel others pain rather than separating myself from their issues, but that's just how I am.  I like emotion.  Good and bad.

Aye aye aye... it's time for me to put this pad away and bid you all a good afternoon.  Back to work for a while before going home to work for the rest of the night.

Peace, and ciao,

Shane

=== Monday April 26, 2004 ===

Sunrise to sunset...

Well I saw the new apartment this morning.  I say new apartment because I'm hoping fervently that the application will be accepted.  It's a very, very nice apartment.  Very high ceilings, a workable kitchen, nice living room, a large deck out back, and a room with a portion of it in brick  I'm already hanging something on that wall that will look good.  I'm already putting up bookshelves and filling them with more books that I'll find downtown.  So, I fell in love with the place.  Very much.  It's got great energy.  It's all freshly painted, and the deck will be painted this summer.

Other than that, I'm very, very tired.  As I've probably mentioned before, I'm on pager this week.  I got my first page at 9:00 this evening.  It went for a couple of hours.  But, it was a good experience.  I've embraced it because I know they won't all be like that.  Not even close.  So, right after I finish here, I'm going to try and sleep for a while.  Hoping that I sleep for longer than a while.  Try to keep up this positive energy for as long as I can.  Because it's going to be a very long week otherwise.  I'll singlehandedly push the price of coffee up a few cents.

Peace Y'all, and sweet dreams,

Shane

=== Sunday April 25, 2004 ===

Downtown, where the lights are bright...

Well, it just might be happening, and soon.  Tomorrow morning my roomate and I are looking at an apartment downtown.  Right downtown.  A walk to the St. Lawrence Market, a walk to the Eaton's Center.  A walk to everything, really.  Used book stores, Union station, restaurants, clubs, coffee shops.  (But then again, there aren't many people not near a coffee shop of some kind these days).  I'm already sold and I haven't seen the place just yet.  My roomate already took a look.  Described it.  It has a deck too.  A large deck for bbq's and the open air.  (Or smog as it may be in Toronto).  It's change, and I can smell it.  It's in the air.  And maybe some of what I"m smelling is the Summer on it's way, or Spring already here, or... who knows.  It'll be good to be closer to the heart of the city.

Anyway, other than that... this week promises to be exciting... in the bad kind of way.  I'm on pager for work this week.  That means fitful slumber, and, well, being on call at all hours of the day/night.  Yay me.  But, that just means the week will be for either working or sleeping, just to ensure I get enough sleep.  Oh, and I'll try and eat in there as well.  I've really been unable to write anything of substance lately.  Except for the odd 'moment of clarity', nothing.  I think partly, it's because of where I'm currently living.  I'm looking forward to the move.  I'm looking forward to knowing for certain that there will indeed be a move.  I may find out tomorrow.  Cross your fingers for me.

Peace,

Shane

=== Thursday April 22, 2004 ===

All my life's an Ocean

Always waves.  Always, always, waves.  Fluid ups and downs.  Needless to say, these last few days have been good days.  Calmer days.  Peaceful days.  Even at work.  Got through a wall at work.  A 'trouble ticket' I was working on with a client.  Personal victory.  It ended up being a problem on their own systems and not our software.  Fancy that.  I crave the ocean.  I crave the wind.  I crave the summer-black night sky far away from the city and 'trouble'.  Below Orion, standing on his head each night, and me wondering if maybe it's me standing on my head and not Orion.

There's been rain, and that's bringing growth.  And that's bringing an ease of spirit that's been missed and is quite welcome now that it's here.  Last summer was bittersweet, as some summers often are.  I learned a great deal about how I've changed over the years.  How I want to change in the next few... or, rather, how I want to grow.  Getting taller's no longer an option.  I left that dream behind.  5'6 and a half is it for me.  I've accepted that.  Last summer I began talking with someone who opened my eyes a great deal.  Brought things back into my life that I had burried.  Beliefs.  Dreams.  Hopes.  I know!  Me, dreamer/idealist that I am burries the odd one under gravel once and a while... but the thing about gravel is, it's easy to slide to the side, to uncover the dreams again.

The moon is growing again.  I wonder if I'm so closely linked with the moon (even if it's just in my head) that my moods wax and wane alongside it?  There may be gold in them thar hills, but I think I prefer the energy in that thar Moon,  the peace of the stars, and the air by the sea.

She used to be a shooting star,
flying oh so fast,
She fell to earth, a comet's tail,
With wings of frosted glass.

I'm aching for a really, honest to goodness, decent digital camera.  Right now I have a few things I need to get.  Except, I"m the kind of guy that would forgoe getting a new perscription for my glasses for a couple of months if it would mean getting a digital camera now.  I hate not being able to capture things I see (with any quality) save for the memories in my head.  And I'm not a good enough visual artist to paint or draw what sits in my mind.  It's all very frustrating.  I like that I can write what I see from time to time, emotions too, but there's something to be said for capturing beauty visually as well.  I wish I had that talent.  I could ease the pressure in my mind I think, if I could do that.

If, if, if. Sure, easilly said.  But, I do draw from time to time.  Paint, ink.  And, I do get release from that.  I guess I just wish I could better portray what I intend, rather than just going to the page with the intention to do anything and have something grow from it, but unintended.  It always feels more like fluke.  Maybe everything wants to be something.  You know, like in carving or sculpting.  The wood has a shape hidden within, and the clay have a shape within as well.  Sculpting is something I enjoy a great deal.

We'll see.  We'll see where this road goes.  Summer in the city.

If I could be where you are,
if I could sing that song
I'd be that man.  I'd be there,
and I'd be whole.

Well, lunch is over for now.  I'm feeling good.  Teh creative side is waxing with the Moon.  The mind is aware.  I am aware.  Peace to all of you, and sweet dreams too.

Yours in truth,

Shane

[Posted 4/22/2004 at 2:47 PM]

=== Tuesday April 20, 2004 ===

Faking It

You know,  I've been working where I am now for almost a year.  It's gone very well.  I've achieved a great deal since I've started, learned a great deal, and met some great people.  And almost every single day I go to work, sit at my desk, and wonder if they'll catch me.  If they'll finally realize I'm faking it.

I say that only because it's how I feel sometimes.  That I'm faking it.  Playing it day by day, filling a role I'm not meant to fill.  That one day they will find me out, and unmask me for someone who doesn't belong there.  I have this fear, this feeling, this something that keeps telling me it isn't me.  I don't know what it is.  I don't know why it is.  I don't know how to handle it except to keep on going.  Day after day.  Now tell me, because, as I always say... if I'm feeling it, I can't be the only one.

Is this a common feeling?  Am I just reaching an age where I'm struggling to come to terms with 'life' compared to life? I have these ideas, beliefs, dreams, thoughts, passions and I just don't know.  I feel almost like I'm just acting out a role.  Filling in until my actual role gets to me.  Just playing bit roles until then.

Anyway, I should get to my dreaming.  Sleeping, and recouperating.  Today the wine club had an Australian Shiraz, and an Italian Chianti.  Both very nice wines.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 4/20/2004 at 2:0 AM]

=== Monday April 12, 2004 ===

Dream:  Make it long, make it true, and make it fun.

I wrote the above line regarding my hope for dream that night.  A long, true, and fun dream.  I guess it had been a while since I had dreamt a truly epic dream.  Now, I don't know if I can every really get the entire point across with me and dreaming.  How much I love to adventure in that world where things just aren't as they are here.  Where I'm in control, even when I'm not.  Needless to say, each night since I wrote that line, I've remembered my dreams.  Much of them, anyhow.  I've also started writing down what I know in a notebook.  It's hard, sometimes, but I let my mind go over and over the dream so I remember.  The epic dream I had the night I wrote the wish for a long dream is a good basis for a story.  I want to expand it, so for now I will not share it's contents.  But I'm hoping I can get myself to write more than my usual short poetry or simple entry and put a story together about the dream.

So,sweet dreams to you tonight.  Enjoy the frolic, romp, or adventure.

Be well,

Shane

=== Saturday April 10, 2004 ===

Lost Days and Waking Dreams

Last weekend my best friend took me out for my birthday dinner.  After a long day on our feet, we were looking forward to settling down in a place called Gypsy and the Hooch.  We arrive after a streetcar ride, in front of the building and reach for the door.  *rattle rattle*.  Closed.  Okay we say, we'll go to this other great place called Bif's.  It was highly recommended after a previous dinner there she said.  All across the city once more, we arrive, weary, hungry, and ready to settle down for a nice meal.  *rattle rattle*.  Closed.  We begin to wonder if maybe Sunday means no restaurants are open.  Which seems strange to me, since I thought many people would eat out on a Sunday.  We scramble to a payphone and go through the book.  She points one out and it rings a bell with me instantly.  Hy's.  According to my parents, an excellent restaurant with excellent steak.  I make a call, and a human being answers.  "Yes, we're open and serving dinner until 8:00."

It's much closer and we make our way towards that Shangra-la to have one of the best restaurant dining experiences in downtown Toronto to date.  So, to anyone in the Toronto area, I definately recommend Hy's.  Now, the only thing is, I didn't have the steak.  I've been trying to cut back on red meat on account of how horrible I tend to feel after eating it.  I love red meat, but I'm beginning to wonder if it's the best thing for me.  Once and a while, maybe.  I instead had the Blue Marlin.  My God, it was beautiful.  Never have I loved fish as I loved that.  If I could have a fish like Marlin every day, I definately would.  It was very solid for a fish, which I like.  Akin to swordfish, and shark.

Now, I find myself at home for Easter.  Much of my Mom's side of the family in comapany, which is nice.  It's been a while.  It's been too long.  It's sad how sometimes disagreements get the better of us.  Bring us apart far longer than they should.  Life is too short to spend any more time apart from those we truly love than we need to.  I guess it's easy for me to say.  I'm the kind of person that forgets the bad stuff of the past.  Water under the bridge.  Sure, it may seem like it leaves me open to being taken advantage of by those who have a mind to.  But, I'm not an idiot either.  Some things aren't worth remembering, and if the person is sincere, I can forgive most things.  Today and tomorrow.  Those are the things we have left that aren't just memories in our head.

Anyway, I should be getting back to the party.  We just had brunch, so we're all a little drowsy, and my brother and I have a chess game to finish.

Peace, and have a great weekend everyone.

Shane

[Posted 4/10/2004 at 11:43 AM]

=== Tuesday April 6, 2004 ===

It's not unusual, to be loved by anyone...

I can't imagine anything different.  I mean, I can imagine different things, but this was meant to be.  This is meant to be.  I get so excited over the small things life has to offer.  When you think about it, even the big things can be broken down into the small things.  It's like energy being able to be broken down into baser forms.  Heat being the basest form.  I think emotion is like that too.  And I feel all emotions tend towards love as energy tends towards head.  It's just a thought, but I like that thought.  A natural state we all subconciously seek to reach.  Mutual love and acceptance for who we are and who others are.  Because the true state exists between two people, or, rather, one of the better states for the human condition.  Belonging.

What would you do for love?  What wouldn't you do for love?  And where would you draw the line between one kind of love and another?  And what would you do if it was too late to change from one kind to another?

It's such a complicated emotion, and so simple as well.  So damned basic and complex at the exact same time.  It's like seeing a solid dot from far away only to zoom in to see millions of smaller dots making up the larger dot.  That's love.  To me.  Or, rather, part of how I see it as existing.

Anyway, it's far too late for me to keep up any kind of sophisticated discussions.  Especially after the conversations I've had with the group I spent my evening with.  We covered politics, religion, all the way to love and relationships.  And a tradition has been born.  The wine club.  Born from a 2001 bottle of Kittling Ridge's Cabernet Sauvignon and a package of the little moo-cow flavoured cheese cubes.  Nothing like cheep wine and cheese to get an evening going.  It's okay though, I'll redeem us next gathering with a nice Italian vintage and some sharp Romano.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 4/6/2004 at 1:26 AM]

=== Saturday May 29, 2004 ===

Unspoken, unwritten...

These past few days there's been so much I've wanted to write about.  So much going on in my mind, and I've had no idea how to put them to the page.  Nothing 'creative' really, more slices of life.  I don't know why it's not coming out.  Why I can't just start typing and letting the words come out as I want them to flow.  As much as emotion can bring thoughts to the surface and words to the page, so too can emotion cloud the method, and the means.  Like being caught in the headlights.  Just sitting here with the blinking cursor, knowing that every single thing I type will be inflicted on the perfectly pristine page.  To marr or beautify the surface.  And I'm not much into marring, but you know, it's necessary sometimes.  Sometimes you have to write it all.

That's part of why I think I haven't been able to write these last few days.  To write thoughts down make them real in a way.  Not just something thought or imagined.  It gives them form.  A kind of substance.  It makes them here to be read.  And I've never really had a problem with that... except, it not only makes it real for everyone reading the words... it makes the thoughts real for me too.  It means I have to think about things more, and confront things also.  And to be perfectly honest I don't even know if there's anything I need to confront... it's just, writing.... I just haven't been able to put words to the page.

I just finished watching the first episode of Six Feet Under.  I'm a big fan of the show.  The emotions that run rampant in each episode fulfil my constant need to absorb said emotions.  And I think that's part of it.  I'm an emotion addict.  Not necessarily my own emotions either.  I crave emotional stimulation.  I need it.  Shows like Six Feet Under definately keep it coming.  I bought the first season on DVD.  I imagine I'll buy each season eventually.  Just one of those things.

Now, let me ask you this.  I've wanted to be a psychologist for some time now.  In fact, when I first left high-school it was what I really wanted to do before I convinced myself that computers would take me where I wanted to go.  I love exploring the mind.  Develepmental psychology holds an interest for me, as does the study of dreams in relation to life and personalities.  How we dream, what kinds of dreams we have, and why.  And I know it's never too late.  It never is.  Except, for me to get to where I'd want to go in Psychology, I'd need to become a doctor in Psychology.  That's quite some time in school.  Which I don't mind, because I like to learn... it's just, I'm so damn impatient sometimes.  Oh, I'm a man of patience with other people, just not with myself.  I'd rather be there now.  But yeah, I know it takes work.

I'm really babbling right about now.  Things have started to drift into routine.  I've always hated routine... but I've always become addicted to them also.  Until they built up to such a point where I'd have to make some big changes in life just so I didn't feel so trapped by life.  Routine has such a 'safe' feel to it.  It has such a 'comfortable' feel.  It also has such a 'oh my god where did the time go' feel to it.  And as time concious as I am, it bothers me.

But really, I think I'm going to go for now.  It's just the Saturday night thoughts starting up for this month.  The first quiet Saturday I've had in a while.  A little bit of solitude always does this to me.  When the sun starts to set.  Maybe I'll get creative and put to poetry some of these thoughts and feelings.  Maybe.  It's also been a long time since I've meditated.  All this change has been good for me, but so fast paced.  Deep breaths.  Baby steps.  Peace.

I'll see ya when I see ya,

G'night,

Shane

[Posted 5/29/2004 at 8:38 PM]

=== Tuesday May 25, 2004 ===

The impression that I get

Well, I've still been settling in to my new home.  Unpacked the last box, did some laundry, put books, cd's and other 'stuff' on my shelves... pending organization.  Last night I got to thinking.  And me thinking when the moon's not even yet half full is a bad thing.  Ah, the past.  It's so untouchable, but so very, very reachable.  I began looking through photographs for inspiration in my writing.  Of course, with the inspiration came emotion and memory.  An almost crippling sense of loss, and an inability to go and visit even for a moment, any part of my past save for the faded photographs and vivid memories.

But, that's not really what I wanted to talk about today.  What I wanted to comment on is the fact that many people have stated that I'm a mystery or enigma.  I don't think this is intentional at all, but it leads me to share a poem or perhaps self-fulfilling prophecy I wrote in a grade 11 text book quite some time ago now:

I am simply an enigma,
changing every day
nobody knows just who I am
not even I can say.

So, perhaps my sub-concious mind has taken control since then.  Perhaps I've been locked in this mystierious path.  What I want to know, really, is what I can do to change that for people who read my writing?  For people who read this site?  Am I a mystery because of what I do or don't write?  Is it simply the nature of writing online?  Is it the single picture of my eye that greets readers, or anything else?  Just let me know, what can I do for you, to unravel the Enigma that is, apparently, me.  I do try and write openly about myself and my past.  Why not, I say, when this is such a faceless forum.  So let me have it.  Let me know what I should do to clarify the enigma... or, let me know if I should go on being just as I am.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 5/25/2004 at 3:23 PM]

=== Saturday May 22, 2004 ===

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/change.jpg]

Ch-ch-ch-ch-changes....

Well, it's Friday night and I'm about to head to bed.  It's a long weekend here in Canada, but I'll be working this Monday so I can get a day and a half off sometime of my choosing in the future.  It's not so bad, but it does mean that I won't get to have this Monday off.  Tomorrow I plan to go adventuring in Toronto.  So much to see, so little time.  But enough time for exactly what we're all meant to do and see.  At least, that's my optimistic view.  But I have to admit, it's very easy to be optimistic while things are going well and much harder to be so when things start to go sour.  Just something to note.  I'm a fairly optimistic person, and I try to be that way even when things are going south.  (Not to say that South is a bad direction necessarily, but since I'm from the north, not having a cold winter would just be weird).

I'm kind of out of it, but it's mostly because I've been hanging out with a couple of people from work, enjoying a little bit of alcohol, and waxing phillosophical.  It's when I ramble... but at it's finest.  So, Victoria day on Monday, and Canada day coming up quicker than you can blink.  Now, I'm not egotistical, or ethnocentric really, but I'm glad to be Canadian.  I'm proud to be Canadian, and I love to celebrate it also.

My gameplan  tomorrow is to first go to the St Lawrence Market, pick up some fresh fish, meat, and veggies, as well as some custom made Mustard and possibly some cheese.  Then I'll walk north a little bit to home, drop it all off, and go in search of some shopping.  Old books, knick-nacks, and some gadgets while I'm at it.  Hit a couple of new-age stores, explore the alleys I come across, and smile all the while.  This is my town.  This is where I live.  A city lad.  Finally.  At this time in my life, I think I'm going to enjoy this.  Later in life, I'll enjoy my bed and breakfast, and the different people that I'll meet along the way.

The bed and breakfast.  This is my dream.  Somewhere on the east coast, overlooking the ocean, this gothic/old style mansion with many rooms.  A hotel almost, but homey.  Big dining room, bed and breakfast.  Salt water in the air, ocean in sight, and ahh, that would be the life.  You see, the ocean's called to me ever since I first tasted it's lifeblood.  It's called to me even before that.  I remember writing a story about a shark in grade 1, before ever having gone to the beach.  Before ever feeling it's life or power.  I used to dream that I'd be taken to an underwater kingdom.  Be made a merman, and forever live under the water.  Some of my favourite dreams are of flying, yes, but the other favourites are of breathing under water.  Those are definately neat.

So, the ocean is where I want to end my life... when such a time comes.  It's just a place that represents so much more than myself.  It's depth, width, and breadth.  Constantly changing, and always affected by the phase of the moon.  Wonderful.  Well, I'm ready for bed.  Sweet dreams to you all, and peace.

Shane

[Posted 5/22/2004 at 1:12 AM]

=== Friday May 21, 2004 ===

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/t/gar.jpg]

Nothing set in stone...

Well, I thought I'd write a little bit about myself today.  Many already know pieces of me that I've shared over time, but I figured I'd introduce myself to those that have not seen those bits of writings.  Besides it gets me to think about things when I do this, and while not always a good thing, it's something I need to do from time to time.

The title, nothing set in stone, pretty much sums me up right now.  There are about two dozen forks in the road soon to be converging on me, and right now I haven't decided which to be walking down when the time comes.  But I like that.  I'm a last minute person.  Just ask Mrs. Kolbe.  I'm an inovator.  I'm at my best at the last minute, and she says that I should put things off to the last minute on a regular basis, because it's when I really shine.  So there High-School!  So there University!  I wasn't just procrastinating, I was living up to my potential as best I could.  And it is interesting to note, some of my best work has been last minute work.  I think it's why I have to start putting myself in a position to have more deadlines with my writing.

I'm a lover of knick-nacks, old books, and photographs.  I remember going through some of my Mom's friends apartments when I was younger, and there was only one that I fell in love with so much that I have a picture in my memory of it's layout.  Even the view from the back, and the fact she had ice-cream in her freezer for when I came to visit.  I think her name was Pauline, and I don't know how often I went over, but here's the scoop.  Little knick-nacks all over the place.  A bead curtain over the kitchen entrance.  And antique things around.  There was just a sense of warmness in that place, and I don't know if it's where my love of those kinds of things stem, but it's a strong and pretty early memory.  I think I was 3 or 4.

There's something about old books.  The faded 'Ex Libris' with signiture in front of some volumes.  The 'To Kathy with love's" that fill the inside covers.  The comments throughout at times, and the fact that they've been owned before.  They have a history.  Someone once held this book, read it, and had their own oppinion on it's contents.  The same is true when looking through photographs.  The fact that someone took the time to take a picture of whatever it is.  The fact that it's  a window into something that happened long ago.  A kind of time-travel.

Just another kind of being conflicted.  My love of new things, gadgets and such, and my passion for old things near forgotten.  Buildings too.  There's so much history everywhere.  We're breathing air that's been recycled through plants over time.  So, old and new.  What can I say.  There's so much to enjoy in life... why be choosey?

Things I want to do in life.  Go back to Australia, visit Eastern Europe, and the East.  Go to Africa.  Skydiving, spelunking, biking across Canada, own a bed and breakfast, write a few novels, poetry volumes, vignettes of life.  Read as much as I can, buy old and new books alike, and build the house that I'll eventually turn into the bed and breakfast.  It's design will be gothic-style mansion, stables out back, the claw-foot bathtubs and portraits of family on the wall.  Or up the stairs.  Have a family, have grandkids, and hopefully see my great grandkids.

So, as you can see, I've got a few things to check off on my list.  I'm sure there's plenty more... but one thing comes to mind on how I'm a procrastinator.  I truly don't want to start achieving these dreams only at 75 and on.  Maybe some things shouldn't be left to the last minute.  Tell people you love them if you do.  It's never worth finding out that it's too late.  Some last minutes are bad ones.

Well, I should start getting ready for work.  Lots to do don't you know?  Tomorrow I'm going to go to the St. Lawrence market, then I'm going to explore Toronto... or begin to explore.  There's so much to see here.  The city's alive, and I love the energy.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 5/21/2004 at 9:20 AM]

=== Thursday May 20, 2004 ===

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/TheStair-grey.jpg]

I stand atop these stairs in darkness
waiting for the echo of your feet
and the familiar sound of plank on plank
a tired house giving way to your passage.
I remember when these walls first rose
our newest home, our jubilance.
For years we marvled at the view
the lake, the road, the marketplace.
For years we warmed ourselves by fireplace
the crackling of the logs at Christmastime.

And now I stand atop these stairs in darkness,
wondering where the colour went
and why it left so quickly,
Having taken so many years to be painted.
For all our trying, building, yearning,
planning, loving, joyful smiling,
nothing lasted longer than our eyes could see.

And nothing lasted longer
than our minds could comprehend.

And so I stand atop these stairs
the darkness all around me
soon these walls will shelter others
and I'll move to closer quarters
just a basement apartment, true
but much, much closer now to you.

Shane

=== Tuesday May 11, 2004 ===

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/t/IMG_0013.JPG]

can many faceted feelings tell the truth?
or do they ponder forever
the resonance of their twins?
secret souls, lovers in the night
dreaming each other to life
living each other to death
and existing long beyond either

i dream your birth, and we are one
no divider between us
no physical restriction, nor
her nor there
we melt and mingle
filter through the mesh

i loved you long before I loved myself
and didn't know where
or how you were
but i've come into my own
and you have to let me know

are you the butterfly's dream,
or the dream's butterfly?

shane

=== Monday May 10, 2004 ===

Served Cold, but not Revenge

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/STA_0002.JPG]

I taste your absence here, in the work that I do, the life that I live now.  I taste it in the English Breakfast tea, and in the Borscht I have at lunch.  I taste your absence here, and it's stronger than it's ever been.  This is all we'd ever wanted.  A life for ourselves.  And it's not so much regret as remourse, and it's not so much a sharp pain as a throb, and it's not so much a stormcloud as a drizzle.  But choices made cannot be undone, only lived.  And paths walked can not be unwalked, only left behind.  It only hits me once and a while, how much things have changed.  So here's to better days, to you and to me, and here's to the memories made, and never forgotten.

Peace,

Shane

=== Wednesday May 5, 2004 ===

Life Behind a Camera Lense

This is how it is.  All my life, at all the family gatherings, when the camera was taken out for those special events, it's almost always been me behind the lense.  I feel comfortable there, and I love capturing the moment.  I hate posed shots, everyone facing the camera and smiling expectantly.  I love the candid shots of life being lived.  A family smiling and laughing together.  Arguing over which christmas tree to pick and cut down for Christmas.  The love, the anger, and everything in between.  I've always felt, either with the written word or in pictures, that I had to capture life.  Emotion.  I don't know why that is, but I don't really care why at this point.  I think it's about preservation.  Of myself and the things I find beautiful.  People and things.

You see, if I preserve what I find beautiful and present it for the world of the future, that much more of me survives into that future.  It also helps me remember myself the way I am now... for when I look back down the road.  It's easy to change little by little and not realize that you're doing so.  So that's why I also like to take pictures, record sound, capture movies, and write.  I write to preserve.  Myself and the world around me.

I just got out of the shower, and I"m pretty much headed to bed, but this thought hit me in the shower so I thought I'd share it.

Peace, and sweet dreams,

Shane

[Posted 5/5/2004 at 12:14 AM]

=== Tuesday June 29, 2004 ===

Seasons they turn, and then they turn again...

I was going to try to write a poem about time and how fleeting it is.  I'm constantly reminded at how fast the first part of my life has gone.  Despite being full of memories, they are behind me now.  So fast.  It feels like yesterday.  Everything feels like yesterday.  And the only thing that I can truly take for fact is that all of my memories are not happening right now at this moment.  I mean, how can we prove without a doubt that yesterday happened?  I mean, with the advent of technology, I guess we can.  But purely biologically, all we have of yesterday or 10 years ago is the same.  Our memories.  Oh, our bodies age, our skin changes, our eyes get those laugh lines.  Those crows feet that today's media apparently feels we should hide.  You know, I find those kinds of eyes amazing.  The kind that have the crowsfeet, because it's usually from a lifetime of smiles or laughter.  Why try and stop or erase time's hold on us?  Oh sure you say, it's easy for me to say.  I'm not fully there yet.  I was only born in 1980.  While this is true, I challenge you to look in the mirror and really like what you see.  The grey hairs?  Love them.  What's wrong with grey hair??  What's wrong with crow's feet?  What's wrong with a wrinkled forhead?  And for heaven's sake, no botox.  If that's even how you spell it.  Not that I care if I misspell the name of that poison.  Gimme a break.  I get so angry with people trying to change how they appear.  At least to certain extents.  Wanting to keep one's self in shape is one thing.  Cutting into your flesh to lift your face, or certain augmentations... sigh... it just raises steam with me.

And now I've gone so far away from the topic I wanted to touch upon that I don't even know if it would be right to sneak it in here.  I wanted to write down some more of my memories that are my earliest.  The whole 'it feels like yesterday' thing.  Okay, my mind's going down that track again.  Maybe I will.

It feels like yesterday:

+++

It feels like yesterday my dad and I were walking somewhere from somewhere, and it started to hail.  We had just crossed a bridge, and I remember wanting to go down to the water of the river, but couldn't.  It was fairly stormy.  I remember being carried on my dad's shoulders that day as well.  It started hailing, and I remember we were crossing a street towards some store.  Probably 7-11, which is a large memory place of mine when I was a wee lad living near Gage park in Brampton, Ontario.

It feels like yesterday that my Mom used to walk me home from school with my brother in a stroller.  Once and a while we'd stop at a park, and sometimes she'd push me on the swing.  I always loved the swing.  Always felt like flying to me, when you closed your eyes you could almost forget you were still tied down to the ground.  Sometimes we'd alter our routes home from school.  Some kind of pre-school, because I was around 4 or 5 at this point.  Maybe Junior Kindergarten.  One route would take us past this house that had so many gnomes on the front lawn.  I used to think it was like some fantastical place.  Not that I knew what the word fantastical meant, but I always loved walking by and looking at all the layouts of the gnomes and garden 'jewelry'.  One time on the way to school, we walked over the traintracks near my house and there was this hill.  I broke away from the sidewalk in a run and went to stand at the top of the hill.  Only... it was an anthill.  And they were crawling all over me before I noticed and freaked out.

It feels like yesterday that I experience my first rainstorm.  Or, rather, my earliest memory of rain.  I guess it kind of explains why I love rain so much.  My first active memory of rain is when I was at Canada's Wonderland, now 'Paramount' Canada's wonderland... which always struck me as funny.  That we even call it 'Canada's Wonderland' still when it's owned by Paramount now.  Which kind of explains why I hate that the Americans own it.  It's my earliest memory.  And I treasure it.  And it's not that I have anything against Americans at all... rather, it's that I have something against whomever sold it in the first place.  It's ours and I want it back. *pout*.  Needless to say, my earliest memory is of me and my family and some extended family at Canada's wonderland.  I only remember that it began raining.  That I was under an umbrella of a tall person.  And that my Father and I went into the cave that was 'Smurf Villiage".  I loved it.  I was two.

It feels like yesterday that 'that' kid first gave me the finger.  I was in kindergarten, innocent as never since, and some kid came up to me.  He asked me: "Can you hear this?" while extending his middle finger upside down.  I of course shook my head, because frankly, I couldn't hear a damn thing.  Then he went on to state "Well let me turn it up for you." after which he rotated his hand so that he was now giving me the finger.  He then laughed and ran off.  Imagine my confusion.  I mean, I still couldn't hear a damn thing!  Crazy kid.  I'm pretty sure I asked my parents what that meant when I got home.  Probably much to their horror.

It feels like yesterday.  These and many more of my earliest memories feel like yesterday.  My schooling at St John Fisher's school in Brampton.  My preschool before that when I lived at 4 Joseph st in Brampton.  My life even before that at the ages of 3 and 4 while living at 95 charlais boulevard.  I remember it all like it was yesterday.  The way the janitor would give us candy when we picked up garbage for him.  For one full bag of garbage at St John Fisher School, I'd get a pack of gum.  Usually, I'd share it with my friend Wilson since he'd be helping me fill as many leaves as we could into the bag... you know, to fill it out. :-)

I remember a little greek girl telling us all that if you closed your eyes in a certain part of the playground, and said in your mind that you wanted to go to this 'other' place, you'd go there and could never come back.  A place where you were always hunted.  Always chased.  I could never bring myself to do it... I don't think.  Though as I've stated before, my dreams for as long as I can recall them, consist of me being chased by something... in one way or another.

I remember being in love with a girl by the name of Jennifer at St John Fisher school.  Only in Kindergarten, I fell in love.  Looking back, I don't know if she felt the same way, but it was doomed to failure anyway.  I mean, with my move to Australia and the fact that both our friends would try to keep us from playing together during recess.  Not that we'd always get pulled away from each other.  Sometimes we'd get to pretend we were unicorns in the field, just grazing.

So far, all of these memories are of and previous to my being 7 years old.  Before I moved to Australia.  There's a whole other track of memories just waiting to be said.  I just keep going over them from time to time in writing and in thought, because well... they're all who I am.  Who I've become.  And for now, I think I need to sleep.  It's been nice going down memory lane with all of you.  In our next adventures, Shane finds himself going into the next door neighbours house through the window.  By invitation of course, and freaking out his mother, who couldn't stand her 5 year old boy wandering all over the neighbourhood all the time.  Without saying where he was going. :-)  What can I say?  I've always been a wanderer.

Peace,

Shane

=== Wednesday June 23, 2004 ===

Sometimes it rains... sometimes it doesn't...

So, I'm in a bit of a dry spell for writing lately.  I've kind of been trying to consolidate my writing now.  The poems I've written in the last two years.  I have them here and there.  Mostly there.  And there's quite a few of them.  Most of them leave me feeling a bit blah in that I think they need some work, but I'm in a 'collect' mentality right now.  Collect the poetry together.  Collect the pictures together.  Store.  Archive.  Reflect.  Redirect.

So, for now, I'm just wandering through memories and writings of the past.  Memory lane, the written memory lane, is an interesting place.  It's different than following memory chains.  It brings me back to the words themselves.  The emotions can come back in this way, but it's the words, separate from myself now.

I think that sums me up pretty well.  A man of many words.  The thing of it is, it's a good thing maybe, but also a bad thing.  It's like living life from behind a camera.  You separate yourself from things around you.  And I don't even know if that cliche holds true for my writing.  It's usually from me, not even observing.  It might start from seeing life around me, but it always comes back in some way or another to how it is affecting me.

In any event, the words are still there... it's just they're not aligning themselves in the right way for me to document them with any grace or fluidity.  They're blocky and separate.  Fractured.

Well, I'm going to work on consolidating my writing now.  Peace to you.

Shane

=== Monday June 21, 2004 ===

Drowning in Memories

I watched the movie Big Fish this past Saturday evening.  It's a good movie.  A tribute to a father.  A good movie to watch the night before Father's Day.  It caused me, however, to start my 'memory chain' that I often go through.  It's something I do from time to time... and I think it might have something to do with why I remember so many things that have gone on in my past.  Family, friends, places, songs that were playing on the radio, what was on the tv at the time, smells.  I think it has something to do with the fact I exercise these connections in my brain so often.  As I said, I don't live in the past, but I often traverse those threads of history just to remember.  I don't want to forget.  The fact that I get to exercise these synaptic connections might have something to do with how much I can remember.

Needless to say, after watching Big Fish, I began along one of those threads.  And I kept on going.  Memory after memory.  I'm afraid that one day, there will be more and more I can't remember.  I think it's why I write down so much.  Often, something I've written years ago; or a picture I've taken, will bring back the emotion and memories of the time.  I love that the brain works that way.  That we can remember as if it were yesterday the things that are long gone.  It can be painful sometimes, but it's a great thing to be able to do.  By remembering the things in our past, we can keep the good things alive in us.  And by remembering the bad things that have happened to us, we can acknowledge that those times are over, and that we've either grown from them, or not grown from them.  From those thoughts, we can take action.

I wonder sometimes if I'm too self-analytical.  I don't really have anything to compare to.  I don't know how many other people do these kinds of things, but I always bet money that I can't be the only one.  Keeps me sane.  On the flip side, the feeling that I can't be the only one can filter through to ideas that require action to complete.  Books unwritten, thoughts unacted upon.  Feeling that I can't be the only one to think something can keep me imobile sometimes.  Frozen with that thought.

Well, whatever the case may be, I have some work to get back to.  I had my interview today for the position within the company that would have me doing the more programming oriented problem-solving which I enjoy.  While I didn't get the job, the interview went well and no doors have closed by any means.

And that's another thing!  Doors.  Bridges.  I've always been told not to close doors.  But picture this.  You're in a hallway with so many open doors around you.  All because you've kept them all open.  What good is an open door if you don't eventually walk through one?

Something to think about..

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 6/21/2004 at 1:55 PM]

=== Friday June 18, 2004 ===

You have to start somewhere...

I guess when you're in a position where you don't have a clue where you're going... you should just start walking.  When you think about it, it's much better to start walking and end up somewhere even if it's not exactly what you expected, than to not start walking at all.  Just standing there, going nowhere.  I feel like that sometimes.  I know it's because I haven't found or started along the path to my 'true calling', however, I think I'm still walking.  The job I have right now is going well.  Yes, it can be stressfull, but it's okay.

I had a conversation with a friend of mine once.  Actually, we weren't any more than aquaintences really and that's my fault.  I was strongly introverted, and only talked once and a while.  He was big into art, and I was doing a computer-science degree.  I told him, I don't know about this.  I don't want to be stuck in something I don't enjoy... really enjoy.  Even if it pays well.  He replied that I was lucky to be good at something that also had the potential to bring in money.  That I should stay the path. Stay the course.  I argued that I would hate to be stuck in a rut like that, despite the money.  It's tough, because to me, money sucks.  I hate that we need it.  I don't know if I agree with him, even now.  It's not that I've fantisized the 'starving artist' lifestyle.  There's different degrees of unhappiness.  I've been happy in every single crappy job I'v had up until this point because I've known I wasn't my job.  I was a write.  I am a write.  I'm not what I do to make money.

Now though, I'm in a good job... not a crappy job.  I'm in a job where I'm being recognized for my efforts.  I have potential futures opening up for me along this path.  It scares me.  I fear it because I don't want to be 40 looking back at my career and realizing that my dreams, my passions took second seat to my job.  My life are the things I'm passionate about.  My writing.  My family.  My friends.  My Photography.  But I guess my life is also the money I need to survive.  It's all about the 'things'.  It's an addiction.  Spending money.  It's like over-eating comfort foods.

Stop the world, I wouldn't mind taking a break.

Back to work.  Peace.

Shane

=== Sunday June 13, 2004 ===

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/goingdown.jpg]Going down?

It's been a calm weekend.  I'm on pager this week.  Pager isn't nice.  I ache for next Monday.

Oh.  And I think the world is out of control.  Some of the things I hear on the news these days horrify me.

Sometimes I'm not sure if I'm dreaming or awake.  How the hell can people do what they do to each other?  Envy?  Is the core of these problems envy?  A kind of jealousy mixed with greed.

Money, land, sex, love, power.

What is power?  The ability to influence?  Or, the ability to remove things that are envyable so you don't have to envy any more?

Should control-freaks be in power?  And as spiritual as I am, I don't think religious zealots should be in power.  It blinds.  Love of God can be just as blinding as love of another sometimes.  If it's the wrong kind of love.  I know I sure as hell don't know better.  But then again, I'm not running any kind of country.  Just myself.  It's not complicated.  If you are a Christian.  A Christian anywhere... how can you justify murder of anyone?  And then again?  In a day and age where having a good defense isn't enough... what's the alternative?  With different groups wishing an end to our way of life, what paths are left to us?  Martyrdom?  Just sitting here and waiting?

I used to think some things were black and white.  Don't get me wrong, I've always been a shades of grey person, but I thought that at least some things were black and white.  Right or wrong.  I'm not so sure anymore.  We're in some kind of river in flood, and all the steppingstones are grey.

The following are the 'Golden Rules' or core rules from what I've learned of many different religions.  So similar.  We all have the same goals I think.  Mostly.  It's the differences that raise this anger in some of us.  It's just so frustrating to me.  To see all this pain in the world due to beliefs being different.  Especially when at our cores, it goes against much of what we should be believing.  And please, I'm not trying to preach or rant here.  I'm trying to get it straight in my own head.  The why eludes me.  And it's the one question I just have to keep asking.  Why?

Christian:
Do unto others as you would have done unto yourself.

Wiccan:
An it hurt none, do what thou will.

Hinduism:
This is the sum of duty: do naught to others that which if done to thee would cause pain.

Judaism:
What is hateful to you, do not to your fellow men. This is the entire Law; all the rest is commentary.

Buddhism:
Hurt not others with that which pains yourself.

Zoroastrianism:
That nature only is good when it shall not do unto another whatever is not good for its own self.

Taoism:
The sage has no interests of his own, but regards the interests of the people as his own. He is kind to the kind, he is also kind to the unkind: for virtue is kind.

Islam:
No one of you is a believer until he desires for his brother that which he desires for himself.

Sikhism:
Precious like jewels are teh minds of all. To hurt them is not at all good. If thou desirest thy Beloved, then, hurt thou not any one's heart.

Baha'i Faith:
Blessed is he who preferreth his brother before himself.

I'm very much a kind of inkwell of spirituality.  My core beliefs are pretty core, but I see so many good faiths and beliefs out there.  You can't sing a song with just one note.  You need many notes, of varying lengths and pitches.  I'll find out one day.  I know this.  One way or another, I think we end up learning how things work.  How they truly all fit together.  But it's the journey that teaches us.  Not some mystical answer at the end of the journey.  It's all the little pieces along the way.

I don't know.  I have to say I've learned and am continuing to learn a great deal in life.  Sometimes it's very frustrating.  Like trying to put a red and green puzzle together while colourblind.  Or a many-colourd puzzle together with many people, but each having a different word for the same colour.

Anyway, I'm off for now.

I hope I didn't offend anyone.  I know there's a great variety on Xanga of bliefs and spiritual callings.  For my part, I've never tried to push my beliefs mostly because I tend to see the commonalities between them all.  Or, rather, I try to.  I guess my core unshakable belief is this:  That there's much around and in us that goes unseen.  That there is more to life than what we can see and touch.

Peace,

Shane Fera

[Posted 6/13/2004 at 3:51 PM]

=== Thursday June 10, 2004 ===

Salutationary Solicitations - A high price for a Hi!

I have so much more to say than meh, but that's what keeps coming to my fingers when I start to type.  Words without meaning.  I'm beginning to think, though, that the only difference between writing I consider good, and writing I consider bad, is a state of mind I'm in or not.  The same words written on a different day might seem far better than another day simply due to confidence or lack thereof.  In writing, I'm fearful.  I think I can admit this now, to myself and to you, that I'm afraid to just write crap.  I'm afraid that Harry Chapin had it right with the singing drycleaner who's dreams were crushed because he decided to try and make it in the entertainment industry, only to be shot down.  He then returned to his town, and never sang in front of anybody ever again.  Now, I know the message of the song by Harry Chapin is that you should sing for yourself.  Be what you are for yourself.  Maybe that's something I've got to get over.  I don't just want to write for myself.  I want to write for people.

+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

ashes,
meant for rising from.
your voice is missed
with slanted sun
against yellow walls
when an Autunm
turned to Winter
turned to happiness.

ashes always
leave me thirsty.

+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

It starts with a word, and keeps going into emotion, and keeps going into memory or desire.

And I desire.  I desire so much.

But most of all, I desire clarity of purpose.

+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

I could write my future in a thesis:

Dreams are a way to give ourselves clarity, if only we would listen.

Sleep, therefore, due to it causing dreams, brings clarity.

Clarity then, comes through sleep.

So, that means, if I really want to find my clarity of purpose... I need only sleep.

Of course, any chain of logical progression can be voided if even one of the points is falacious.  False.  Incorrect.

Do dreams hold grains of truth within them?  I think they do.  For me, my dreams have always brought to light things I hardly thought about at all during the day.  Always in story form, but random connections bringing about the continuing story.  And the most profound dreams I've had have been a couple of dreams where I've met someone within and instantly felt some kind of bond.  A connection.

And, here's my thinking.  If dreams come from within, do I secretly desire a bond with myself?  Or is my mind fabricating a bond filled with such a fervent emotion simply out of illustrating the fact that I desire someone to share thoughts, love, and life with?  That I find myself in that particular situation at those particular times?  And, if there's a possibiliyt that the collective unconcious exists, does that mean dreams may come from without?  Or, rather, that dreams may bleed into each other, or those close to us?

Are any of you familiar with the Schuman Resonance?  It's the magnetic field that exists in and around the earth.  It matches the brain-waves of a human being in Alpha-wave state.  In essence, the earth has a brainwave.  An alpha-wave.  We go through Alpha-wave state when entering and leaving our dream-sleep.  Our R.E.M. sleep.  Tell me some of you are as fascinated by the fact the earth has this resonance as I am?  The earth has an alpha-wave pulsing along.  To me, reading about this, it flared the idea of the collective unconcious right away.  Brought those thoughts to the forefront of my mind.  If that's possible, is it not possible that we all share a connection at that level?  Our subconcious.  Our minds are capable of so much we don't know about.  Or aren't concious about.  Even strong intuition often comes from us just going with what our subconcious mind has already calculated without our really knowing.  I guess I just wanted to explain that I'm always fascinated by science and poetry.

So, it always comes back to dreams for me.  Superficial meanings, deeper meanings, connection, perception, it drives me nuts.  And I love it.  The search for the truth.  My truth.  The search for my truth, and learning.  There's so much out there I don't know.  And I want to learn it all.  And that's where time is not my friend.  But, at the very least, I can keep learning what I can.  In time, maybe I can get to where I'm going.  Or at least, keep going until I can go no more.

Anyway, I think it's time for some clarity, and if my logic holds true, that means I should go to sleep now.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 6/10/2004 at 11:53 PM]

=== Wednesday June 9, 2004 ===

Of inner selves, and outer selves, and the mysteries in between...

Last night was one of those nights where everything is felt.  Everything is heard.  Sleep is far off, and the skin feels like just a little too much clothing.  The heat beat down on the city yesterday, and while it may not have been record-breaking, coming out of the cooler weather, the heat just feels so much more like... heat.  And I hate the heat.  Or rather, I dislike the heat.  When I feel every single inch of my body because the heat presses against me like cellophane paper.  The sheets chaff, and the night doesn't bring as much cool air as I would prefer.  The heat drives me crazy.  I miss my autumn.  Where perfect temperatures exist, and the smells waft through the air of harvest, and full moons just seem that much more alive.

Heat.

The mind can't think, the body can't relax, and the heart just keeps remembering the past while seeking the future.  Some people think of their pasts as chains, keeping them from reaching their futures.  Maybe that is the case for some people.  Maybe.  The truth of it is, the past only exists in memories, and echoes, and consequences.  Yes, we often pay for what we've done in the past.  Good payment and bad payment.  Yes, the past is real to us, but it doesn't exist anymore.

It's easy to say, I can't do this because.  I can't be this because.  All the hurt we've dealt out or been dealt.  I know it stays with you.  It's a part of who we become, but please don't let it ever stop you from going down the paths you want to go down.

I was reading something in a book the other day, about the worst opera singer of all time.

"Some people may have said I couldn't sing, but nobody could say I didn't sing."

It's just, every once and a while I'm reminded of the different pain people go through and are going through.  Sickness, divorce, lonliness, sadness, physical pain, or even their pasts or their lack of futures.  I always feel so helpless.  I'm me, and they're them.  So I write.

The reason I write like I write, about my own pains, and joys, is because I want people to read what I write and maybe identify with what I've been through.  That maybe, some of the problem sometimes, is that we feel alone in our pains and sorrows.  Maybe then, just maybe, everyone wouldn't feel so alone in their pains.  Who knows who reads and what anyone gets out of it, but you know, maybe I'm doing it as much for myself as anyone else.

In any event, my lunch is over, and I'm heading back to work.  Gotta keep up the momentum, right?

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 6/9/2004 at 1:56 PM]

=== Friday June 4, 2004 ===

I've got 10 minutes, haunt me now
you can haunt me now, I'm ready.
But not, not five minutes before...
not 10 minutes before I sleep at night.
When you haunt me when I close my eyes
you're right there in front of me
you're right there
and I can't change all the years gone by
time's measurement may be our creation
but it's passage is beyond our control
don't visit me before I sleep
I can't remember years ago
and drift away like nothing. ever. was.
So haunt me now, I beg you.
Haunt me now.

I had a really bad dream at the beginning of the week about a friend of mine.  I forgot about it until yesterday.  Dreams can be horrible things sometimes.  The things that happen in them so real.  The first nightmare I've had in a while.  I want to post it, but I can't just now.  I have to think about it a little while longer.  In the meantime, tell the people you love that you do.  That you love them.  And I don't just mean romantic love here.  We all have friends we love unconditionaly.  At least, I'm sure many of us have friends we love unconditionaly.  Tell them if you haven't lately.  Time flies far too fast for you to put it off till tomorrow.  I guess the dream was just a reminder that anything can happen.  You don't want it to be even a split-second too late to say those words.  And yes, those that are that important to us usually know that they are that important... but affirmation isn't a bad thing.

Peace,

Shane

=== Wednesday June 2, 2004 ===

you run deeper than you think
and everything you do
all that you remember
what you yearn and hope for
makes ripples in life

You write of childhood and happiness, or childhood and pain, and I feel you.  And while I'll never know exactly all you've been through, what you've gone through good and bad, I feel you.  You affect me.  You keep me writing.  Your life, your existance keeps me going day after day.  Your passions, dreams, and feelings give me hope.  That you can sit there reading this and know I mean you.  That you affect me.

We're all so very connected.  So much more connected than we sometimes know.  These ripples run as deep as we do, and much longer than the earth is round.  There's no way you can feel pain without my feeling it as well.  There's no way you can feel joy without it rippling my way.  And life is hard.  Life is so hard.  Us moving through all these ripples, making our own, and wading through the rest.  It's so hard to know that what we do matters.  That it truly does matter.  With so many ripples out there, how can our own single movements really matter?

They matter.

You matter.

you run far deeper than you think.

++++++++++++++++++++++++

Okay, so I became inspired to write a little bit.  It startles me sometimes, how much sadness there is in the world.  How much pain people sometimes feel.  It doesn't startle me in that 'I don't feel pain, how can people be feeling pain?' kind of way.  It startles me because I think we become so inoccuated against other people's sadness.  It's like a fog sometimes.  It's just there, so desensitization becomes easy.  We adjust, accept, and move on.  Why the hell should I adjust?  There's a reason behind everything.  The grumpy man on the corner, blaming the world for all his troubles.  There's a reason he feels that way.  We've all got these things inside of us that we've kept with us all our lives.  I just dislike how it becomes diluted in the world as it is.  With so much going on, and so much bad news.  You don't matter any less.

I wish money wasn't a necessity.  It's taken us so far from what I think happiness should be.  Maybe some people truly are happy making the money they make.  Living the lives they live.  I mean, I'm not unhappy where I work.  The power goes out, and the world begins to wake up.  Candles get lit.  People start to talk.  Talk.  Don't get me wrong, I'm as much in love with technology and advancement as I am in love with an electricity free environment.  As I've said, my heart is in Coniston.  My home.  Up north, you look around and you see forest.  Rock.  Lakes and rivers.  And believe me,  under a full moon, on a lake, hearing the loons call and bullfrogs test their bass voices... nothing has ever had me feeling so alive.

And I guess when it comes down to it, these are just my own opinions.  I know that not everyone feels the same way.  It's just me being egocentric sometimes.  Believing that if only people experienced some of the things like that.  Nature.  Raw and uncut.  A starry night, shooting stars.  Life as it was.

Progress.  Sometimes that word makes me cringe and sometimes it doesn't.

I thought about this before.  And it comes into context because in all these times I've been in nature, I've known I was going to be heading back.  It makes it a little more intense.  In a way that on a very cold winter's day.  A bitterly cold day, wher eyou can only cough-breath when you step outside.  Sometimes the only thing that makes it bearable is that you know you're going to be walking from one warm place to another.  You know the cold won't last for you.  But picture this.  You've been walking in a bitterly cold winter day, and you know that when you stop walking, that's where you're going to sleep.  That's where you're going to stay, bitterly cold, until you get up (if at all) in the morning.  Then it becomes a different kind of cold.  No hope of a warm place at the end of your journey.  Maybe that's why I can feel as passionate about my 'nature' experience.  Because I know that it will end.  That I"ll get my internet back, my music, my 'other' life.

I really don't know.  I know how much I've come to 'need' all these amenities, but I hate that I need them.  It's like an addiction.  I sometimes wish electricity would just stop.  Except for places that truly needed electricity to provide servies to help people live.

Okay, I've been rambling far too long.  It's a full moon I'd wager.  My creative spirit is rising, and so too my passion and longing of nature.

Peace, friends, and sweet dreams,

Shane

[Posted 6/2/2004 at 12:0 AM]

=== Tuesday June 1, 2004 ===

My Grandmother and her House

My  Grandmother is a great woman who has profoundly affected the family she began over 60 years ago.  A woman of unconditional love, reason, family, integrity, and warmth.  She and the house she's lived in for over 80 years hold a large spot in my memories and fond emotions.  From the first lemon merangue pie I ever remember having, to playing a game called 'Spite & Malice' with my Grandmother on a weekday afternoon when it was just she and I spending time together.  Being only 24 years old, myself, I know I've only been able to experience a short sprint of time with my Grandmother.  But, some of the memories of my childhood that I'm going to share have stayed with me since then, and will forever be a part of me.  I'm really not sure how old she is right now, but I hope our family can all be together on her 90'th and subsequent 100'th birthdays.

My childhood was a childhood filled with travelling up north to visit a town just outside of Sudbury called Coniston, Ontario.  And that little town, that small town that saw both my parents grow and become a family of their own... that town is the heart of my childhood.  Despite the fact I've moved all over the place in my youth, it's the heart, the roots of the tree.  It is where the heart is and always will be.

The house is something that I've always loved.  Two stories, no basement, kitchen chairs that never fail to catch big toes, and a baseboard heater I always used to knock the cover off.  Bookshelves filled with Children's 'Book of Knowledge' and adventures of Rip Van Winkle, Peter Pan, and the Atlas of the world.  Figurines, knick-nacks, and doilies.  An antique phone at the entrance, a large tree out back that had the most amazing scent in the fall and spring, and the creaking of the house at night.  Not to mention the trains that would go by not 500 meters from the house.

I want so much to write and write right now, but I'm so very, very exhausted.  But believe me, I have many memories to share of that beautiful white house, and the family that grew within and around it's foundation.  My Grandmother has told me how they built the house from the ground up.  Starting with just one room, and sheet metal for walls no less.  Adding room after room, along with the children to fill them.  Ahh, many stories, but that will have to wait.  For now, dreams are calling me... and boy, I sure have been dreaming these past few nights.  Can't say I don't enjoy the adventure though.

Peace, and sweet dreams,

Shane

[Posted 6/1/2004 at 12:15 AM]

Whether it's art and photography you're interested in, slices of life, or just a gateway to some addictive comics, go check her out.

=== Saturday July 24, 2004 ===

Lucrece

Lucrece is my best friend in 'real life'.  By that, she is not only a Xangan I read, but someone I met long before Xanga.  We became fast friends, and I knew she was the kind of friend everyone deserves, but not everyone gets... and I knew that right from the beginning.  Quite frankly, I could talk for some time about her, and all we've been through, but I'll keep this short.  We've been through a great deal in our friendship, rocky times, and smooth sailings... and through it all we've both known a friend in each other.  Even when we weren't being always 'friendly'.

She's one of the truest people I know.  Constantly herself, without hesitation.  A sarcastic sense of humour with intelligence and wit to boot.  She's a food artist, a chef in the making, and my lord you should be so lucky as to have even a small slice of her cheesecake!  We have good times when we hang out.  From fancy restaurants to just walking around Toronto.  And though life keeps taking us in different directions, we still find time to hang out once and a while.

So give her a peek and say hi.  She hasn't posted in a while here... since I believe her computer may be having problems, but drop her a Xangaline.  She's good people.  The best people.  One of those who speak their mind.  Enjoy!

=== Thursday July 22, 2004 ===

Just Deserts - Just Desserts!

I think I'm going to do something now that I have wanted to do for some time.  I'm going to go through the people that I currently have on my sites I read list and just say something about them.  Some I've been reading for a very long time, and some a lot less time than that.  But I'll start with James.

James was one of the first people I met when I joined Xanga.  Or, rather, one of the first people I began to read.  First I signed up purely because he wrote a little vignette on everyone who became a subscriber.  And I wanted more readership than I had.  That was how it was in the beginning with me I guess.  I hadn't really found my comfort here yet.  I was on another site name than I am now.  "Abaxial", actually, I guess it's still kicking around here somewhere.  I joined when many others began here, with Bianca sending an e-mail and my finding my way over.

James World Airlines took off, and I began to read often.  A man who always seemed to draw many people... some people who often disagreed with him, and many who felt like I did, that his words were wise.  That he wrote them well, and that we enjoyed reading them.  By the time I got to this site-name, I joined him for another reason.  Simply because I liked to read what he had to say.  I still think he's wise.  I enjoy his words, and I think I can honestly say I'm better for having found him here on Xanga.  I don't often comment on his site, though I know a comment never falls through the cracks with him.  It always seemed that he truly notices every single comment.  I've often been intimidated by the mass ammount of comments on his site, but that's just how it is.  He inspires many comments.  His writing and thoughts spark it I guess.

So, if you don't know who he is (and you must, he's kept his name since the beginning.  Same site.)  go have a look.  I promise you'll more than likely like what he has to say.  If not, come back here and demand a refund.  I'll then chuckle and tell you that the advice was free.  (Then I may make a rather obscene gesture, but you're still welcome to ask for a refund.)

Stay tuned for VickyVix tomorrow.

G'night,

Shane

[Posted 7/22/2004 at 12:32 AM]

=== Monday July 19, 2004 ===

sunlight never gave me freedom.
promises of; maybe,
but no freedom or dreams realized
actualized;
only theorized, and maybe agonized after.

a whisp, a wayward thought
i am without form
a ray of light, or shadow,
it makes no difference when
one mirrors the other

i need you to give me structure.
I need form, and resolution.
Beginning and end.  A place
from which my thoughts can be
arranged and understood.

Randomness given order in you.

Ahh, but you have no name or face, a melody maybe, a promise but no structure.  You won't tell me your name, I haven't seen your face, and you play at order like two children at pick-up-sticks.  What direction will you give me when I find you?  When you find me?  When we meet for the first time, or last time, and the planets seem aligned.  Mars in the evening, whispers in the trees.  Saying that I see dead people would be a lie.  But I see memories.  In peoples eyes.  In their actions.  In the way they walk and act.  Our past helps create our future.

But I feel adrift.  I feel like we were supposed to have met already.  And I wonder if this means this one's a write-off?  Trees fall in the forest every day.  And while I can't hear them, I remember them.  They leave their memory behind in the sprouts that shoot up in the aftermath.

If not now, then later, yes.  I understand that.  It's all about circles, and cycles, and what comes before leading to what comes after.  It's all about patterns, and lack of pattern.  About how random it all seems, and how very not random it all is.  To say I love you is not a lie.  Love is so easy, even when it gets hard.  It's not the love that's hard to deal with.  It's always the reprocussions of that emotion.  Love makes waves.  Love makes for stormy seas.  Love makes for wind and hail, and passion between the elements.

I believe in the future.  How could I not?  When you think of the future as a mix of tomorrow, the next day, the next year, the next thousand years, and the next million after that, it's hard not to believe in the future.  I think all things seek balance.  And eventually, all things find balance.  And like the odd particle that escapes from a black hole, there are sometimes those things that seek to go against balance, to fight it, but I believe in balance.

So I guess we'll see.  I've got patience.  Too much, some would say.  But I feel that I've got all the time in the world sometimes.  With some things.  But I love this life. I love every single breath of it.  I believe in what comes after, but I'm enjoying what I have now.  I believe I'll get there in the end.  There are people waiting for me to get there.  But time is a funny thing.  Time is absolutely infiniite.  We've got all the time in the universe.

You exist with a purpose, just as I do.  Grasp it, believe in it, act it.  There are no such things as useless people.  Unimportant people.  You all know the image of the tapestry of life.  I like that imagery.  One thread going astray means the whole pattern being marred.  And I don't believe that happens.  All things for a reason.  And pain?  Pain is so here and now.  I like to watch drama's as much as I like to watch comedies because my emotions get played.  They remind me that right now, right here, I'm alive.  I'm living life.  I'm feeling.  I'm very interested to find out what comes after, but I can wait.  Here and now are all that matters for this moment.  Finding purpose or acting upon it.  It's easy to find purpose in things when you look back.  Because you know what came out of certain choices that you've made, and other people have made.  The hard thing is believeing in the purpose of the moment while you're living it.  Because we cannot yet see the outcomes of our actions.

I guess this has turned into another 'Just Live' blog.  I can't help it I guess.  I believe in things.  I believe in all things, together.

Well, lunch is over, back to work.  I guess my purpose today is to help a client with their computer problems.  And my purpose tonight will be to dream.  And then write about it all in the morning.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 7/19/2004 at 3:3 PM]

=== Wednesday July 14, 2004 ===

"Stickshifts, and safety belts..."

It's no secret... I'm no secret really.  It's hard to hide things in words... at least, I see myself so clearly in the words I write.  But, it's because I know myself, and my reasons for writing every single thing that I write.  When I really think about it, it's different for all of you reading what I write.  You read just the words.  And that's something I have to remember when I put my pen to the page, or keys to the keyboard.  I write and you only get to read the words.  I have to show you what I 'feel' in the words I share.  I have to show you what I think.  What I don't think, and what I want to think.  What I dream and what I fear.  And I picture myself at the end of my life looking back over all the things I've ever written, and it'll be me.  All of me on thousands of pages in hundreds of journals.  Jumping back and forth between them with no linear timeframe.

I don't want to feel that I have to wear a safety belt in life.  I don't want to be strapped in and 'enjoy the ride'.  I want to be standing from the car as it's moving, shouting (still) to the sky, waving my arms in the air and smiling, laughing, and crying all at the same time.  I found out today that I believe I have charisma.  I'm good at selling things one on one.  I have a quick-start personality with less fact-finding or follow through, and I'm good with my hands.  My personality type in the Kolbe Index is Inovator.  I work best last minute.  But that's besides the point.  I often leap before fully thinking about a decision, which is funny, because of how indecisive I used to be.  Less so now, believe me, and I love that I'm growing away from indecisiveness.

I choose life.  I choose it.  It may or may not have been my choice at the very moment I sparked into existence on the earth, but I sure as hell choose life now.  Just watch me.  And you know, I can't wait for my vacation.  I'm taking time off from August 4'th to August 15'th and going north.  Almost to Sudbury, but to a cottage on the west arm of Lake Nipising.  Where the sky is black at night, and the stars light the way.  Where the mountains are oldest, only rocky hills all around, and life sings loudest to my ears.  Where I first fell in love with everything that didn't exist in the cities I grew up in.  Where I could hear the earth breathing in response to my own breath.

I didn't learn my words up north, but I learned my silence.  I learned my respect.  I learned that when you watch, things happen.  Magical things that may have their explanations in science, but never cease giving me a sense of childlike wonder in how it all happens.  How it all can go about happening in the first place.  A plant is a plant.  But oh no, my friend, a plant is something that forces it's way out of the ground.  It reaches forever towards the sun, which it can never reach but keeps trying to do.  It's cells come together, and lower than that, it's molecules, and even particles made up of tiny strings (if you believe in the Superstring Theory) vibrating.  Making music.  Ahh, the music of life never had so much meaning as up there.

So I'm going to disappear for 10 days.  I'm going to bring my camera, I'm going to bring my childlike wonder at life, and I hope I can bring myself to finally jump off of black rock.  Something that stands 25 - 30 feet out of the water.  Something I couldn't bring myself to jump from over 5 years ago.  But... I want to do it.  I'm ready to jump.  I have to test my wings.

Goodnight all of you.  Happy Wednesday, and in answer to CazzaC's question that she posed her readers, I don't pronounce it "Wed-nes-day" when I'm speaking, but always pronounce it that way in my head when I spell it.  Because I'm horrible at spelling.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 7/14/2004 at 11:13 PM]
