=== Wednesday November 17, 2004 ===

I dream of Jack while waking

My Jack Kerouac collection came today at work.  The complete audio collection of Jack.  Listening to his spoken word, wondering where my words go when I speak them.  First week of escalation pager.  It's not a bad time.  It's not as bad as being on the front line.  I have to get up at 3:00 AM tomorrow to make a change on a system, and to make sure a different client is doing okay.  And I have no problems with that, because my words set me free.  I'm not a computer jockey, spelling support to clients calling constantly, me climbing the walls.  My words set me free.  I'm not trapped in this body of flesh, nor laden with untruths, because there is only truth.

A lie is just a mask that a truth wears.

And these words keep coming to me in a constant stream.  Why I'm free.  Why I care, and don't care.  Why I can fly and flutter, and float.  Why my passion is possible.  Why this girl I like at work gives me butterflies and smiles all at the same time.  As much as a beautiful smile, and observant eyes.  As much as a beautiful smile, and beautiful walk makes me sigh.  It's the mind, it's the mind that gets to me.  The intelligent questions, picking my brain when it would rather lie dormant some days mid-week while I'm wearing my lethargy like a housecoat in the office.  It's those glistening, sharp eyes that see things beyond the surface of this world.  Who ask questions that need answering that I never thought to ask, or cared to answer.  That's what really gets to me, and keeps me up on a November 16th when I should be sleeping.

And right now, just right now I'm going for a flow of thought on paper.  No stop between my mind and my written word.  I need to dump these letters as they come.  They are who I am after all.  And I can't deny I'm in need of spelling out my existence on every blank page I come across.  And I'll be damned if every time I click the 'new entry' button, I'm faced with another one to fill.  And I know I write as much for myself as anyone that may be reading.  In fact, I write completely for myself, but with that is attached a complete love of the fact that my words are read by those I want to be able to read them.

I grew up learning that words could shape worlds.  The wizard of Oz taught me that any world was possible.  Return to Oz taught me that people who visited such worlds were often thought of as crazy and visited psychologists.  And my life since then has taught me that it's the crazy ones that never visit those worlds, and the sane ones that keep going back again and again for fear of losing that true reality that exists when we imagine, dream, wish and hope just a little bit.  And I'll never stop dreaming, and imagining.  I've met too many interesting people this way, I can't go back now.

You all smile so brightly when you smile.  I've gone blind a thousand times over in my life.

And it's your eyes that smile brightest of all.  And then again, they are the windows, and windows never did much good keeping out the light.

Sleep keeps tapping me on the shoulder, but I swear I'd love to just keep rambling forever and a day.  It doesn't seem like long ago I was sitting at a friend's kitchen table, writing a story about a shark after school in Grade 1.  Last minute homework before the father came home to ensure my work was done.  I would be sent to bed after dinner right away if it wasn't... and let me assure you, it was never done completely enough to warrant not going to bed right after dinner.

And while that may be a little bit of an exaggeration, it is one of my more vivid remembrances from childhood.  The past that never leaves me of how school was the most important thing to my parents from the time I started Grade 1 till the time I started finding my own self in grade 11 and 12.  Yes, a long time to be pushed along in such an overpowering way.  I agree.  Maybe it's why I'm so listless, and directionless at the same time.  Maybe it's why I don't have a clue where I'm going, and why I think I half like that fact.  And maybe it's why I developed such a vivid imagination.  I never could stand those realities of dreading my homecoming from school to face questions about why this and why that.  To face more parental homework of write this and write that.

And you know what?  My biggest feeling of guilt about anything I felt growing up is the fact that whenever my father would go on business trips, I would be the most happy child in the entire world.  I feel the most guilt about that.  He used to travel a great deal, so I grew up with him being home and not home.  And I remember clearly my mind doing double-time on the nights before he would come home, planning my answers to questions I knew would come about school and my work, and anything else.  I would anticipate conversations ahead of time, because he would always ask why this.  And are you sure that.  And it drives me nuts that my past still bothers me this much at 12:00 on a November 17th, 2004.  That at 24, I'm still thinking about my growing up, and how much some memories still bother me.

My relationship with my father now is a great one.  I couldn't wish for better.  And I've brought up the past from time to time because I just wish once he would say sorry.  Or acknowledge that maybe he was too strict.  But it never goes there when I bring it up.  It's brushed off and fluffed away, and I'm left with these unresolved memories and emotions from a time when I feared my father more than anything.  And dreaded going home.  We have a great relationship now and I can almost talk with him about anything.  We have different political views, views on life, and many others, but that never gets in the way.  Our shared passion is movies, and games.  Strategy games mostly.  We talk business, because I know he loves his job and the business world.  I can live with the past, and even it being unresolved I guess, but I'm sure I'll write about it from time to time just for my own peace of mind.  And I'm confident that my own particular plan for parenthood will be something a little different than how I was raised.

And wow.  How can I go from talking about Jack Kerouac and go to my personal past like that... that's perhaps something that needed to be written then.  Everything for a reason, right?  And it's okay, because this is protected anyhow.  I think the ramble is rumbling to a close and my eyes are closing too.

Peace to all of you, And sweet dreams,

My your own fuzzy or sharp memories of yesterday be at peace with your soul, and any harsh pasts and personal particulars fade into a happier now, and an even happier future full of all the possibilities that can exist.

Shane

[Posted 11/17/2004 at 2:30 PM]

=== Sunday November 14, 2004 ===

2:00 in the Garden of Good and Evil

I Just finished watching the remake of Stephen King's 'Salem's Lot'.  Stephen King's stories often involve struggles between good and evil.  On top of that, the evil often takes on a kind of 'satan' figure, or ultimate evil incarnate kind of body.  Any movies regarding this particular struggle always piques my interest.  It tugs at me in that certain way that wakes me up, keeps me there, and leaves me there long after the movie has finished.  The thing about Stephen's stories and the good and evil struggle, is that the hero figures are often flawed themselves.  And I know there are all kinds of literary terms for this kind of hero figure.  I think hubris might be related.

I guess this ramble isn't about much I guess, except my faith in life and in people.  People in life will sometimes let you down.  That is inevitable.  But I think that a person is more than just a choice made in accordance with more variables than you could imagine.  All things for a reason, and the people we are underneath ourselves maintains some kind of 'average' or 'balance'.  No matter how far lost we may sometimes get, we're never so far lost that we lose ourselves.  We remain inside, underneath it all.

Again, I don't know why this is all in my mind right now.  Some things have to be said at certain times for often reasons unknown to us at the time.  I've found that our actions in life are often for others, even when we think they're for ourselves.  If that makes any sense.

I think I'm very tired right now, and I may not be making much sense.  Even to myself.  So I'm going to sleep now.

See you all later,

Shane

[Posted 11/14/2004 at 2:7 AM]

=== Tuesday November 9, 2004 ===

A Mid-November Night's Poem

Puck am I,
Perhaps.
I am change,
bringing dew.

Do you desire
Misty mornings?
Summer Midnights spent
Outrunning the sun and
Chasing the moon.

Seek not tomorrow now,
stay with me here.
In our twilight of the soul
Eternal.

You'll be the Nymph,
and I'll be the Satyr.
Salacious, Loquacious,
Playful and bright.
Our magic is right,
in heaven, tonight.

+++Shane

=== Sunday November 7, 2004 ===

No, really.  Because I just don't know.

Life.  Yes, yes, I know.  This tired old subject that's often on my mind.  The art of wanting more.  Is that what life's all about?  I say to myself, if only I had this one thing, everything would be set.  THEN I'd really be living.  And it seems, each time such a thing is achieved, all that's left is a brief moment of elation, and then more questions.  A constant climb and fall.  I just don't get it.  I feel like I'm constantly living contrary to myself.  That I love and hate everything I have or do.  It's driving me nuts.

Does getting recognition where you work make any of you feel like you're just getting sucked in deeper into a world you never wanted to exist in, but got pulled into?  And I don't mean in the moment.  Recognition, and climbing the corporate (in my case) ladder feels good in the moment.  Except, not as much any more.  I sit at work and I want more.  I know I've written about this, but I was talking to my dad a couple of weeks ago and actually communicated this to him as well.  That I feel like I'm heading swiftly to a decision.  One that will have me either dive in to the business world or one that will have me take a 180 and dive into the arts.  I told him that because he's big into business, and I suppose my subconcious wants him to be aware that it might happen.  That I might just one day up and 'quit my life' so to speak.  To dive into something new.

I know that business and art doesn't have to be mutually exclusive, but I find myself being totaly unmotivated when it comes to the arts.  At the end of the day I'm mentally weary.  That's why I used to enjoy working in a factory.  Physically I was tired, but mentally, by the end of the day I was dead on.  I would think all day about what I would create.  Poetry written on scraps of paper at break and lunch, thoughts drifting around all day.  But, I do remember then.  Still that feeling of not 'having' it.  I knew it wasn't where I would end up.  Just a stop along the way.  And I'm looking around and wondering how many stops along the way there will be.  And wondering when I'll get to the stop that lasts more than a little while.

But I'm whining.  More procrastination, because I started working on a website.  I've got a headache in the make, and I'm wondering if there's any connection to my inner thoughts and the fact that I've had rough headaches for the past couple of weeks off and on.  Change of weather maybe.

I unloaded my camera today of pictures. A friend's car.  And cakemix.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/CarSide2.jpg]
[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/CakeMix.jpg]

Shane

[Posted 11/7/2004 at 7:10 PM]

=== Thursday November 4, 2004 ===

Beat's Me (Pad 2 - 02)

Drinking the froth from the milky way,
I soar high
above the toadstools
and swampy swill
forcefed
factory thinking
mechanical inspiration
driven in

I never had a plan
and that's my song
I never could stand
to adapt to the doldrums
life kept throwing me
my ankle's protected

you can take away my ears
but not my hearing
my eyes by not my sight
my voice, but not my words.

You cannot hurt me here
not a prison, but oasis
of starry delight
swallowed whole
in the milky moonlight.

+++

Shane

=== Friday December 31, 2004 ===

On Youth; we who lack credentials.

A comment someone has made recently (I think in a friendly way) has caused me to remember prior times that similar sentiments have been spoken about my ideals.  The naivety of youth.  Those four words in the past have been spoken to me by someone I used to work with.  This person was roughly 20 years older than me, a Pisces, and had lost all faith in people.  All people except children.  He trusted nobody, and constantly told me I'd eventually be just as cynical as he was.

The naivety of youth.  It puzzles me, really, that it's naivety to believe that this world is a beautiful place despite the shit that exists everywhere.  That the people that populate it are generally good people, with their own loves and passions and lives.  If my constant state of awe at everything around me is the naivety of youth, and if complete cynicism is the 'everythings eventual'.  If that's what stepping away from youth truly is, then please, label me an eternal youth and absolutely naive.

The fact is, I see the crap, I see the anger, sadness, and even ugliness of parts of this world.  But isn't it naive to begin to let those parts of this place become your reality?  Isn't it naive to just believe that because youth is behind you that you have to stop seeing the good?

I've met a great deal of naive people in my time.  Youth, Elderly, and middle aged combined.  I've also met a great many people who have the solidest feet beneath them, but haven't lost sight of the clouds their heads used to be in either.

And it truly isn't the most recent comment that set me off on this thread, because from what I can tell it was friendly and benign.  But it was definately the memory of one of the last people to say those same words to me.  The man who forgot how to believe in anything at all.  And almost, even, doubted that the sun would rise tomorrow.

I'll tell you what.  Everyone, just have faith that the sun will rise tomorrow (Except those in the far north who are currently in their 4-5 months of darkness.) and if the sun does happen not to rise, I'm fairly certain it'll be too late to worry about it.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 12/31/2004 at 1:40 AM]

=== Tuesday December 28, 2004 ===

It doesn't matter... because YOU matter

I'm not going to pretend I'm not human.  I'm not going to pretend that things do or do not hurt me when a hurting thing is done.  When dealing with other people, there's always some hurting I think.  Because as much as we try, we can't truly look out from another's eyes.  I don't pretend that I can.  But one thing I can say and I try always to maintain, is that you matter to me.  I have a good memory for some things, but I think I remember good things more than bad.  We go through our life, and we do a combination of good and bad things.  And we find ourselves here, at this one point in time, with all these 'things' behind us.  The truth is, at any one point, I believe that we're not what we've done in our life.

We're never the people we were yesterday, as much as we can sometimes trap ourselves into thinking that.  It becomes so built in that we live and breathe it.  We turn in, and we fold in, and we just go along the mobius strip, eternal circles spiraling inward.  But the truth is, if you stand right now and close your eyes, and think about your life.  All of it.  The good and the bad.  You are not your past.  You are you.  Yes, we are everything that has made us up to that point, but the power lies in us to take a step forward and understand that anything we don't like about what we may have done is in our hands to move away from.

I believe that it doesn't matter because WE matter.  I believe that I've often trapped myself within my past, and I also believe that it doesn't have to be that way.  Each breath you take is one breath away from the last moment.  You can never change the past, but you can direct your future.  It is all about choice.

And that's why the Pheonix and it's story means so much to me.  We are all pheonixes, and we rise from our own ashes each moment, day, and year.

Happy Holidays everyone, I hope you all enjoyed yours.  My own holidays were good, if not long enough.  And perhaps not filled with all the people I'd hoped they would be, but I believe that each day brings us closer to those people we'll meet again in life.  And beyond this life.  I guess that belief helps a little too.

We are all connected.  (As much as I hate that that phrase has been turned into a mass marketing slogan for a certain phone company, I have always believe the phrase.)

Peace, and Happy New Year, (back to work for me now)

Shane

[Posted 12/28/2004 at 12:42 PM]

=== Thursday December 16, 2004 ===

Red Perfection

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/Pommegranate.jpg]

I'm here.  I really am.  I'm reading, and sometimes commenting, but I'm tired and I haven't bought anything for Christmas yet.  Last week was a pager week that put all my others to shame.  I'm also not yet done Fountainhead by Ayn Rand.  It's caused me to be introspective, but in the good way.  I'm close.  So very close.  Some acts of personal courage take time.  I love Christmas season.  I love the nighttime.  I love the chill but not too biting wind.  The crisp air, and ice.  I love that my brain is only giving me pieces of fully formed thoughts to work with right now.

There are so many things I love, and so many people.  How is happiness not here, right now, in this moment?  Pieces of happiness can be found in each moment, just as surely of pieces of sorrow can be found in those same moments.  Sometimes it's a conscious effort to make yourself go one way or the other.  Sometimes it hurts so much to guide yourself as such, and other times it's like coasting down a hill that was particularly hard to cycle up.

Life is that pomegranate above.  Life is very red.  It's a red thing, this physical, raw, life.  It's encased in layers, and each sweet taste contains a seed that might be hard to swallow.  It's a marvel to see it slowly unfold as you go it's path, and as each layer is unwrapped, beauty.  And things are left behind, but the memories stay as the pomegranate's stain on white.  Life is so very red, and that's for passion and for pain.  Encased in sometimes bitter layers, and always beautiful.  But it's made up of so many single, decadent moments.

I love pomegranates, and I love life, and I fully believe that when they're left behind me, fading memories;  I'll miss them both.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 12/16/2004 at 11:16 PM]

---

=== Monday December 6, 2004 ===

Crazy Diamonds, and Wishing you were Here

As I spend the late evening writing these words while listening to Pink Floyd, I can't help but wonder.  About things.  All things.

I had fun this past weekend on Christmas Tree Day.  It was a lot quieter than the past few years, but the people I invited from work, as well as a couple of other friends did fill out the party quite well.  Poker, Drinking, Games, biting winds and a Charlie Brown Christmas tree at the end.  Don't get me wrong, there's nothing wrong with the tree, except for it's diminutive stature.  Kind of short.  But nice.  And no, I didn't get pictures, because I forgot the camera here at the condo.

I'm right now just experiencing a bit of a flux.  Or a non-flux.  A state of non-flux is where I am currently at.  Lord help me, I'm not going to stay here.

I'm just right now missing certain people, and certain possibilities which I believe to no longer be available.  Certain dreams dreamt at inconvenient times definately help to bring those feelings to the fore, that's for sure.  You know how they can sometimes go.

++++++++++++++++++++++++

Be Here Now

We're just two lost souls,
swimming in a fish bowl,
year after year.

You told me you were it,
that you were all I'd need
against the coming winter
with longest, darkest nights.

I held you close, certain.
Sure that my breath
was the only oxygen,
the only heat you needed.

I still see that line of light,
against the wall;
A jackhammer of a
memory held dear.

The rising sun, and
rising passions.
Our twilight of souls,
entwined in this life.

Running over the same old ground.
What have we found?
The same old fears.
Wish you were here.

+++

Shane
(Compliments to Pink Floyd - "Wish you were here" for the italicized portions.)

=== Friday December 3, 2004 ===

You moved me, and now I've moved myself

Well, I'm officially in a new place of residence for a while.  I moved from my downtown apartment back to Scarborough, where I spent 3 months living on a couch in a nice condo.  Things have improved now, however, as I get my own room with wall to wall and floor to ceiling windows on one side.  I love it.  It's clean.  Nice view.  Right next to the Scarborough towncenter.  Right next to the subway. (5 minute walk).  Pool, squash, weight room, badminton, table tennis, sauna, hot tub.  All the amenities.

I moved on Wednesday.  I walked around at work like a Zombie on Thursday.  I feel refreshed today.  And tomorrow is the Fera and Friends anual Christmas tree hunt.  For those of you who have never heard me talk about this Christmas tree hunt, I'll give you a rundown.

Christmas Tree Day, as I like to call it, is always the first Saturday of December.  Without fail.  It always consists of my immediate family, and anyone else who shows up, going to get a christmas tree.  Sure you say, sounds pretty tame, normal, and festive.  Oh, it's festive all right, but not tame and possibly not normal, but let me explain.  We go out into the woods, and it started out just my brother, mother, father, and uncle.  The next year after that, two friends of the family came with us.  Then another uncle the next year.  And so on.  The point is, now it's upwards of 15 or 20 people that show up every year.  This year's even more due to the co-workers I've intruigued.

We go out into the woods, with two 'water' bottles filled with black zambuca.  One uncle has a bottle in those inner pockets that winter jackets sometimes have.  And my dad usually has the other one in his inner jacket pocket.  So different people take turns throughout the christmas tree hunt sucking back some zambuca from these bottles.  Some people more than others.  When we get back with the trees, they stay outside while we amble (yes amble) into the house for my uncle's famous chili.  Then, as tradition goes, we pour some shots called slippery nipples.  More zambucca, then with baily's layered on top.  They're kind of easy to drink.

By the end of the night, there's usually someone who has passed out early, but there's lots of catching up, and having of good times.  I'm a fan of these annual family get togethers.  I know I've posted things on my family before, and I may write descriptions of it's members someday, but right now, I hadn't realized that it would take this long or that I would write this much.  I have to get back to work before the work fairy comes down and hits me a couple of times.

Happy December people, and I'll write more later.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 12/3/2004 at 1:21 PM]

=== Sunday January 30, 2005 ===

The Inkwell

I wanted to write something this evening that signified my passing from one place to another.  One state of mind to another.  But I can't think of anything at all to write.  Not just here and now, but maybe by the end of these lines I'll have something.

+++

The words I write are from the Inkwell.  You know they are words we all share.  They're words that exist for all of us.  The only thing I do is arrange those words to be shaped into what I see or feel.  A thing is the same to all of us.  An apple.  A basket.  A river.  It is, at it's core, always the same.  But you start writing about a river, and then I'll start writing about a river.  Both of what we write about the river is truth because we think it.  We are both right.

I can write about the river as God.  A mythic and winding thing, waters deeper than the human soul and a path cut from the source of everything to the end of nothing.  I can see the river as this majestic and benevolent entity that is aware.  Because I remember a river and what it means to me from my youth.  Because it means all these things to me.  At my core.

You can write about the river as a Demon.  A taker of life, a malevolent being bent on cutting things away from the land.  You can write of how your brother or friend was taken by it's murky waters and now is trapped in that ever moving convoy into the void.  That you'd never be caught dead walking the banks of the river, for fear that death would catch you.

We can write these two things, believe them with our entire beings, and we'd both be right.  A river is a river.  But it is more than that too.  It is more than just a river because we are not the river.  We stand beside the river looking in and believing the river is one way or another.  And we are both right.  I think there is only truth.  I think that's what I think now anyhow.

Truly.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 1/30/2005 at 11:22 PM]

---

=== 2 Comments ===

One of the best homages to the nautre of truth and reality that I've seen.

{v}

-- Posted 1/31/2005 at 9:37 AM by Naminanu
The interesting thing about words is that even though we know what they all "mean", they don't necessarily mean the same things to all of us.

I think that's the reason for so much bad poetry that's out there.  The poet is simply making assumptions that words mean the same thing to the reader as they do to themselves.

(and yes...I've heard the argument that poetry is all subjective anyway, but I still say that ambiguity of interpretation can be carried much too far, and often is).

=== Thursday January 27, 2005 ===

Self Knowledge
And a man said, "Speak to us of Self-Knowledge."
And he answered, saying:
Your hearts know in silence the secrets of the days and the nights.
But your ears thirst for the sound of your heart's knowledge.
You would know in words that which you have always know in thought.
You would touch with your fingers the naked body of your dreams.
And it is well you should.
The hidden well-spring of your soul must needs rise and run murmuring to the sea;
And the treasure of your infinite depths would be revealed to your eyes.
But let there be no scales to weigh your unknown treasure;
And seek not the depths of your knowledge with staff or sounding line.
For self is a sea boundless and measureless.
Say not, "I have found the truth," but rather, "I have found a truth."
Say not, "I have found the path of the soul." Say rather, "I have met the soul walking upon my path."
For the soul walks upon all paths.
The soul walks not upon a line, neither does it grow like a reed.
The soul unfolds itself, like a lotus of countless petals.
-Kahlil Gibran (The Prophet)

[Posted 1/27/2005 at 9:46 AM]

=== Wednesday January 26, 2005 ===

No Choice but Belief

I think I'll be okay.  The only thing that's going to change entirely is that I'm going to soon make a doctors appoitnment for a physical.  There are some things I need to be sure of about my health.  And while any worries I might have may leave me for now, I'm sure they'll come back from time to time.  The thing is, I want them to come back later, when I have more experience with life.  When I have even more thoughts, and dreams.  When I'm more at peace with things.  I had trouble sleeping last night.  Not at first, I slept solid for 7 hours.  Then woke up instantly. My dreams faded and I lay there, tired but sleepless.  I think far too much.

I feel like the dwarves in the Lords of the Ring.  As they dug too deep so have I in my thoughts, and released a kind of demon.  I may have to sacrifice a part of myself to remove it, but the good news is, there's rebirth after such a sacrifice.  And understanding.  And right now, right here, I am.  There is only today.  As I've always said, to contemplate the next form of life is just like a drawing contemplating what it would be like to be alive.  And since I did keep thinking further, since when you dig too deep, there's no choice but to keep digging until you find the vein of ore you were looking for in the firstplace, I've discovered another line of thoughts I need to hold on to, and maintain.

Each morning when we wake we are reborn.  You've seen me write that before.  Our entire past is only a memory.  Yes, we were there and lived it.  We loved and hated, we did things.  And as I've often spoken about, our remembered dreams are much the same.  They are things we have done in a way.  But since everything that is before right now is just a memory, it is as if every morning we are rising from our past.  Not only that, but perceptions shifts that may happen later will not be me losing my identity.  I don't think so.  Our whole lives from birth to the end are a series of perception shifts.  We're still us.  Just bigger.  And I don't mean physically.

So, I think I'm getting past this thing.  There's no choice but to get past it.  It's rocked my faith a little bit, but I hope I'm stronger than that.  I've had my faith rocked before.  I'm sure I will again.  You can only cross bridges when you get to them, not before.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 1/26/2005 at 8:38 AM]

=== Sunday January 23, 2005 ===

Life (again), the Universe, and Everything

I know I've been absent.  This past week has been a pager week.  Today was an issue regarding a client and file transfers.  Sounds exciting, no?  Well, tomorrow there is a scheduled conference call between them and us.  Us being probably myself since I've gathered all the information on the problem under the sun, then management, and possibly a co-worker or two.

I hate conference calls.  Especially when the client is pissed off, and I'm just the guy who's trying to help.

And on top of that I was reading a book earlier this past week.  A book that's made me think about things and possibilities I absolutely don't need to be thinking about right now.  You see, I have this interest in spirituality and religion.  Well, spirituality mostly but I don't want to get into any issues I have with any religions.  I accept possibility and have an open mind.  Up till this point it's helped me get through the day, but what I read forced my mind to contemplate things that pretty much have made me very much below par this week.

I'm sure it sounds like an exaggeration, and maybe it really is nothing.  It's just, it's hit me like a weight and I haven't been able to throw it off as I have before.

It involves both my biggest fear, as well as life after death.  And I know I've talked about that before, but this book just mentioned other possibilities I never considered.

You know, I really don't even want to write about it at this point.  Not past this point anyhow.

I. Am. and so are you.  Know that with every fibre of your being.

Love you all.

Shane

=== Monday January 10, 2005 ===

The Salmon of Change; When you're high up on a Perch, your Sole feels so light...

So, I've started the new year pretty well.  Began seriously working on at least one of my resolutions.  I've handled it in this way.  Eating less, eating better, and eating better.  (With the exception of the case of Muroc mandarins I ate over the course of three days this past weekend).  But even Muroc mandarins are probably a more healthy choice considering some of the snack alternatives.  But so far, since the new year, I haven't had anything but fish for a dinner meal.  Fish and veggies.  I mean, it helps that I enjoy vegetables.  And I'm developing more of a taste for Sushi as well.  So, so far so good for these positive lifestyle changes.

And, I am starting to go swimming more regularly.  Of course, it's easy in the water.  A swimming pool is no substitute for the ocean, however.  Where the waters live, and where you can wrestle with waves, and feel the earth breathe.  As childish as some dreams can be, I still wish I could breathe under water.  I've always felt at home under water.  Trying to hold my breath as long as I can.  Just drifting face down and looking at the light rays filter through the surface.

I don't know exactly why water has always been that way for me.  If it's because I'm a pisces, or because my parents began nurturing my water side since I was just a baby.  Bringing me into the water at a pool and just dropping me in.  Apparently there's a reflex that all baby's have when dropped into water that allows them to hold their breath on instict.  I've also always been attracted to how quiet it is under water.  Sure, you can hear sound travel not too badly under water, but it's a different kind of sound.  You feel it as much as hear it.

Anyway, I got pulled away during my writing of this, and my lunch is now over.  I'll be back.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 1/10/2005 at 1:33 PM]

=== Tuesday January 4, 2005 ===

Resolutions, Disillusionment, and Convoluted Thought

Well, I've never been one for resolutions.  I've generally been opposed to the idea that one should wait till the new year to make certain positive changes within one's self.  That being said, I guess sometimes a universally accepted time to make positive change isn't a bad thing after all.  Because for many people, it does help such changes come about.  To not be alone in wanting to make changes or resolutions helps.  That being said, there are a few things I want to do this year.  They're not so much resolutions as a 'To Do' list for 2005.  Another reason I've been opposed to resolutions in the past is simply because I have a tendancy to say something and do something else.  My Kolbe profile (a psychological profile) has me tagged as an Innovator.  That includes a very high 'QuickStart' score with a much lower 'FollowThrough' score.  Lots of ideas with a slim chance to complete them without solid deadlines and a taskmaster at my back.

So, let me ask you this now.  Would it be silly of me to resolve to actually see some 'resolutions' through?  A kind of mobius strip of a resolution.  But I've always like the idea of the mobius strip.  It's always reminded me of the snake swallowing it's tail, which is a symbol of the infinite in a way.

So, without much further ado, my list for 2005.

1) Get back in shape.  Before I began my desk job I was in shape.  After I began my desk job, I quickly fell out of shape.  I suppose working in a factory had it's advantages, and I kind of miss getting paid to work out.

2) At least attempt to be published.  I've said this before, but maybe in a resolution format I"ll have more success in motivating my self.  I've got lots of material, and I'm confident I"ll get there.  I just bought an L shaped desk at Ikea I'm hoping will aid in my creativity as I'll now have a place to sit and work on my computer AND by just sliding to the left a little bit, I'll be able to write, draw, ponder, and do that kind of thing.

3) Get my liscence, or at least get on the path to doing so.  At 24, I think it's about time I hop on that bandwagon.  I've never been a fan of cars in general.  I prefer my bike.  But there are times when  liscence will be helpful.  I can always rent a car when I need one.  I definately do not need the expense of a car, but a liscence will help.

4) File my tax returns for the last few years... This isn't just a resolution, it's a necessity.  I think the government owes me some money for most of my returns, and I think I owed them 20 bucks for one year... but I hope to at least get this cleared up before I have to flee to another country.

That's pretty much it for resolutions.  I mean, things like 'Find my true love' is a little vague and potentially unatainable in just one year.  It's kind of an ongoing resolution to end up with a soulmate or twin flame, and a couple of kids.  That's more of a 'down the road' thing I'm hoping for.  I resolve to be a dad someday.

I also do hope to start being around here more often again, with pictures to boot.  Photography is something I've always enjoyed, but I've been a little busy the last couple of months.

Well, ciao for now, and peace,

Shane

[Posted 1/4/2005 at 1:54 PM]

=== Friday February 25, 2005 ===

The Day After Tomorrow... Err, I mean the Day After Yesterday

Well, I officially survived my birthday.  And thanks for the comments and well wishes.  I went out with some friends last night for dinner.  In fact, I share a birthday with another friend of mine from work.  But yesterday was a very, very mixed day.  This friend of mine was let go from work yesterday, along with 8 other people from within the company.  Apparently we had to 'trim the fat' so to speak.  So, it is what it is, and changes come and changes go.  We went to a steakhouse for dinner, and I had a steak.  Now, I love red meat, but I'm finding more and more that it doesn't like me.  I suppose when you condition your body to eat mostly foods that are easy to digest, the red-meat really mucks up the works.

The wine.  We had a Pinotage from a company called 'Two Oceans' from South Africa.  Nice wine.  That's really all I have to say.  Was looking for a spanish wine last night, but the wine list at this particular establishment was slim pickings.

Tonight I head 'home' home for the weekend.  I like to call it 'The town that transit forgot' simply because there's no public transit, and the routes via Go Transit to Georgetown are convoluted and long.  Luckily, I'll be getting a lift in after work.  And that will be that.  25.  One day older, one number higher, but I got this smile on my face because no matter what, it is what it is.

I know I've said I've always been a river, taking the path of least resistance, and maybe for a little while there was a dam blocking my way.  But all a river does when there's something in the way is either rise up to go over, rise up to go around, or rise up to get enough force to break through.  Whichever one I have done, I'm not certain, but I'm headed past the dam and towards smooth flowing once more.

It is what it is.

And the world's so damn beautiful.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 2/25/2005 at 8:30 AM]

=== Thursday February 17, 2005 ===

Say it in Spades - The World is not Enough
================================

A friend recently posted about our competitiveness back in high-school.  I admit it, I'm a competitive person.  I enjoy competing and enjoy a challenging competitor.  And he is certainly a challenging competitor in all of our games of choice.  He raised an interesting analogy between gaming and life.  Back in high-school we played a great deal of Hearts, Euchre, and other games of skill and chance.  I tended to be a big risk-taker in games.  And as he says, it made for some spectacular wins... but he's also probably right about me losing more than winning.  I suppose the fun for me was in the risk-taking.  The thing of it is, for me the analogy is opposite to how I lived my life.  Big risk taker in games, and too conservative in life.  In games there's nothing to lose but the game.  And I'm competitive, but it's the journey rather than the win.  In life, I was shy, didn't take risks, and didn't have any spectacular wins, or losses.

Something I've found though, is that of late my game playing involves less risk taking, but my life is beginning to involve more.  I don't know what that means exactly, except that life is indeed too short to not take some risks for the spectacular wins.  Happiness is important.  Your happiness is important.

I remain zealously competitive, and probably always will be.  I was raised with a strict diet of cards, board games, and video games.  As well as once being a competitive swimmer and avid tennis fan.  In sports I'm more into the one on one competition.  In board games, I'm more into the strategy games of any kind.  I still take risks in games, but perhaps not as much.  But life, life isn't a game and you can't just start over from a save point.  But for a spectacular win?  I think I'm game for just about anything.

As for the infamous 'bottle' incident.  The doctor says a couple of more years and I'll be seeing from my left eye again.  All I can do now is hope and pray. ;-)

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 2/17/2005 at 1:33 PM]

=== Tuesday February 15, 2005 ===

Ray of Light

I walked a mile and spoke your name,
a prayer against the winds of time,
to shelter us, lost souls of fame,
starcrossed, passion our only crime.

And well I know how this will end,
a poison drunk, and dagger thrust,
no message found, and none to send,
the mind will speak, but heart mistrust.

To talk against the breaking wave,
and silence sound with soundlessness,
An act bourne of a will to save
A once bright light; now comfortless.

I fear a loss so great it numbs me whole,
Your gift will everafter wake my soul.

+++

Shane

---------------------------------------------------------------

The above is not in light of Valentine's Day.  Nor is it speaking for or against aforementioned day.  The above was a blurt. Not near finished, and only freshly written.  I know I've often gone 'protected' in fear of my poetry or writing being taken.  But right now it's the farthest thing from my mind.  Today was a good day.  It was a quiet day, and a full day.  I got a lot done, and not enough.

Tomorrow is another day.

I always have a desire to explain my poetry because I often write with very veiled verse about things that I'm thinking or feeling.  I realize that for the mostpart, my poetry has a surface meaning as well.  It's why I always want to explain myself.  And it's why I probably won't for a while also.

In short explanation, the above is a memory, a hope, a fear, and a realization.  All in one.  A memory of a place, a hope of echoes, a fear of consequences set in motion, and a realization that no matter what my life will never be the same again.  For better or worse.  Not the verysame as it was.  And that's a good thing and a bad thing.

So many contradictions eh?  It just is.

I have a day tomorrow to spend with my best friend.  She's my best friend because she is.  I'm sure we were best friends before we met because I swear our first meeting was more like a reunion with an old friend rather than a meeting with a new one.  I joked about it once saying "Old soul greets old soul".  Just an  unspoken greeting.  A recognizing.  We'd both fight viciously for the other I think

And with that, I'm off to sleep.  An early morning, and appointments to keep, and a meeting with a dear friend.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 2/15/2005 at 1:19 AM]

=== Friday February 11, 2005 ===

Friday - Nuf Said

Well, It's Friday finally.  And though I'm on escalation pager for work, I feel pretty damn good.

+++

Uriel Moth stared.  Staring's all you really can do when you find yourself waking up in a place that isn't the place you found yourself falling asleep in.  She stared not only for this reason, but because there was a rather large purple person standing over her as her eyes flicked open, though 'person' isn't perhaps the best way to describe what she saw.  A large purple face looked down on her with a single eye and a hat that reminded her of Captain Highliner from the fish-stick packages.  His silvery eye, shielded by a monacle, blinked as she bolted upright.

"You're awake." he stated in a too-English voice.

+++

It's all about waking up.  What if I had woken up today to find things a little different than I remembered them?  Would I discount these memories as faded dreams from days gone by?  Would I say, "Well, since I AM awake, and this is how it is, I must have been dreaming."  I'm still fascinated by dreams.  There was a short period of time I was terrified of them over the last couple of weeks, but dreams are so much like gateways.  Gateways to what?  That depends on who you ask.  Though if you ask me I'd say it varies.  Sometimes a dream is a gateway to yourself.  But I believe sometimes a dream is a little more significant than that... though perhaps at those times 'dream' wouldn't be the way to describe an experience.

There's so much mystery here.  This place.  It's all we have to hold on to.

I still believe.

Shane

=== Thursday February 10, 2005 ===

Pictures painted

I've painted pictures often in my past.  With words, or charcoal.  Or wayward glances across the hall before a class.  I've painted pictures, swathed my soul upon this canvas stroke by stroke.  The artist hand can show, I am revealed as ever I was.  I line of paint.  A stable memory.  A bellowing laugh.  A smile.  I am fulfilled as ever I was.  Moving foward, as ever we should.

I've painted my name upon the earth with each step.  Branding this or that, defiance at my inability to BE that which I tread upon.  I see the grass, but I am not the grass.  I see the clouds, but I am not the clouds.  With each step I've made a mark that says I am apart from you, the earth beneath my feet.  I am separate.

Rather, I should brand the earth upon my soul.  Mark the wind within my heart, and the sky within my mind.  Each single star, my own light filtered back at me.  Rather, I should realize that though I walk upon the earth, and under the stars, that I am of the earth and stars as surely as the earth and stars are of me.  That I am not separate from them.  That I am indeed the grass, the cloud, myself.  Not branding, but sharing.

We paint pictures often, the universe and I.  As we walk along the beach, our sand in our toes, we paint the moon rising over the horizon.  We paint ourselves with every stroke.  With every step.

We paint each other.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 2/10/2005 at 12:47 AM]

=== Tuesday February 8, 2005 ===

Equal and Opposite

Pager week has a way of putting everything back into perspective.  Brings us back to the very basics of existence.  Action\Response.  There's no pre-meditation or deep thought in it's most simple mechanism.  I get a page, I respond.  I'm on high alert (granted, not at first) and ready for action.  Nothing else matters at that time.  There is only the pager, and the guaranteed customer it is putting you in touch with.  There will be another action\response yet to come, but in a different format.  Problem\Solution.  Yes, a little more thought involved, but when you're waking up after only two hours sleep, there's not much room for anything else.  No other sinister thoughts, only problem\response.

It ocurred to me that this is an easy way to go through life.  React rather than proact.  Let life take you rather than you taking life.  But let me assure you, life should be taken.  In it's utter completeness.  If taking life for you involves working at a job you don't love to provide for a family you DO love, than that is it.  Family completes you.  If you seek the secrets of existence, than that's your bag.  Take it.  It's all there to be taken.

And taking sounds like such a selfish act, but it's not depending on how you look at the taking.  By completing yourself you are completing the tapestry that is everything.  By being completely yourself, you are making sure that tapestry is brilliantly perfect.  Perfectly brilliant.

Oh, I know, I'm getting preachy, but I write these words so that I can read them when I'm not the me I am at this moment.  I think I'm coming to the realization that when I write and 'talk' to the reader, I'm talking just as much for my future self.  To my future self.  And if you want to be included in that discussion, then by all means, pull up a chair.  I'm a friendly guy, and despite my hermitish tendancies, I enjoy people.  All people.  Even the ones I don't really enjoy.

So that's my Tuesday night pager contemplation.  That being on pager (at least when I'm paged) clears my head is a good thing.  I've done some spring cleaning around here.  (In anticipation of srping, and in yearning for the Sun I spent half my life hiding from).

As of now I'm heading to bed, that sweet slumber that slowly seeps silently down to the marrow of one's awakeness.

Catch ya later,

Shane

[Posted 2/8/2005 at 11:42 PM]

---

=== Sunday February 6, 2005 ===

All Across the Universe

Today is a Pink Floyd day.  Or, rather, tonight is a Pink Floyd night.  I'm going to spread my thoughts across the universe and drift off to that place where all our thoughts go as we sleep.  The ones that don't content themselves with the confines of the human mind.  The ones that find other stray thoughts, or the opposite of stray thoughts, and dance with them in the night.  Riding the starlight across the path of the moon and landing gently in that distant western shore where the Elves of Tolkein's masterpiece now reside.

T.S.Elliot came to mind to me today.  A poem entitled 'The Hollow Men'.  I think he was conflicted.  Or, at the very least, I feel that poem came about from some thougths of his own.  Perhaps a spiraling thought.  Images of Ozymandius, and an entire lack of raging against the dying of the light.  The contrary.  Not with a bang, but a whimper.  I think he had fears, or acceptances, and that poem represented many of them.

This past week, in all the downs and all the ups, I've come up with something that I finally understand.  That I know nothing.  I know nothing.  The beginning of everything is nothing.  I hope it is.  I hope that when you lose so much from your own mind that you have so much more to gain.  I know nothing.  I'm not afraid as I was last week, or two weeks ago.  Not at this moment in time.  At this moment I am.  I'm writing here as I didn't think I would tonight, and looking forward to falling asleep to the stylings of an artistic group that inspires me, saddens me, and makes me happy all at the same time.  I'm looking forward to tomorrow, but I'm experiencing today.  That's a step.  Worrying about tomorrow is silly.  I need to understand that.  Worrying about things that are absolutely out of my hands at this one moment in time, preposterous.

This is what I want for the next post I write here.  A different topic.  I need to start seeing again, instead of just looking.  It's funny how things get fogged up when you get too close to the glass.  I need to take one giant step back from myself, breathe, and start to be the person I am meant to be.

Love Is.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 2/6/2005 at 11:12 PM]

=== Monday March 28, 2005 ===

Cayenne Pepper Truly is the Spice of Life[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/HomeSpice.jpg]

I could make up some study that some scientist did somewhere that finds a correlation between ingesting Cayenne pepper and longevity of life, however, I would indeed be pulling such a story out of my ass.  Instead I'll simply state that I love Cayenne Pepper.  It's my favourite spice for spice, so to speak.  And makes up part of the first picture I'm going to shower you of my new place of living.  My new state of being.  The here, the now, the spices on my stove.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/t/HomeSpice2.jpg]

I'm a fan of tinkering.  I'm not a 'cook' by any means, but I cook.  When I do cook, I tend to throw things together and add certain spices that seem to work well together.  Kind of like art, except my roomate is far better at the art of cooking than myself.  She threw something together the other night that belongs on the page of a menu rather than in my gullet after work.  Needless to say, she's real artist when it comes to food.

So why spices to start of a few pictures of my home?  Really?  Because I love spices.  Not to be confused with 'heat' in food, but spices of all kinds.  Sweet, savoury, zesty, hot.  They made the rice I used to almost exclusively eat due to budget constrains sing rather than snore.  And that's important when you're eating the same things each night.  Of course garlic is my favourite other than Cayenne.  Though Garlic is not something I consider a spice.  It's a food like onion is a food.  And Garlic I eat far more often.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/HomeLakota.jpg]

The next picture is of the living room.  It doesn't include a view of the fireplace, but that will come eventually.  Not sure why I wouldn't have taken a picture of it, but it seems there's narry a one on this set.  The living room is nice.  Not huge, but cozy.  And a fireplace as I mentioned.  There's lots of wood in this apartment.  Wood trim everywhere, hardwod floors, I love it.  (Oh, did I mention I'm on pager this week?  Yeah, coming off a full moon AND on pager.  Shi-tay).

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/HomeRoom.jpg]
This is a section of my room on the left.  A couple of my shelves set up, a walking staff behind the halogen ligth carries on it an empty Crown Royal bag.  The staff was a gift from a New Yorker when I was in Scouts and was in New York State for a Jamboree.  I carry it with me because it's sturdy, reminds me of my roots, and reminds me that I'm going somewhere too.  The Crown Royal bag is simply there to remind me that if I get drunk, I'll have the walking staff handy.  The book shelves are in a state of disarray currently, but will work themselves out as time goes on.  Progressing from 'I'll fix them up later' to 'Tomorrow, I'll get to them tomorrow' and that'll lead to 'I like them that way.  It's how I find things.'

I have a bike on which I'll ride this summer.  It will take me to the lakeshore.  That's where the water is, and where the rivers go from here to give themselves.  And water, as you all must know by now, is something I'm a fan of.  Though lake Ontario isn't the cleanest water, it's still a body OF water, and that's good enough for me until I find myself back in the cool and tempermental embrace of the ocean.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/HomeRange.jpg]

On the right now you'll see the gas stove that I'll have to get used to cooking on.  It's hot heat, gas cooking, and I've ambled at it each time I've tried thus far.  Something about it starting to sizzle almost as soon as heat is applied.  And forget about 'low' 'medium' and 'high'.  It's pretty much just on or off.  With a small range of differentiation.  Hey, don't go makin' fun just yet for those of you who cook on a gas range, I applaud you.  I'm still getting used to it, and hopefully will someday learn the art of how.  (Probably around the time I move into a different place that doesnt' have a gas range.  Wouldn't that be funny.)  Lets just say that with a gas range, I've been having to scrub the bottoms of pots and pans a great deal more often than ever before.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/HomeHall.jpg]

On the left, the fridge and entrance to my room.  I like the door, and I hate the door.  The door has a window.  Inside!  And a curtain that is not so thick.  So I've hung a towel on the other side making it opaque enough to my liking.  And the door has a lock on it.  'Nothing big' you state?  Maybe to someone who has ever had a lock on their room door, but I have not.  I grew up in a house that didn't believe in locks on bedrooms. Except parental bedrooms.  The last two places I've lived have seen me with no door on the bedroom at all.  (I like to call that bohemian living).  So I revel in the fact that I can lock my door at will.  Just as long as I don't lock it and leave, since there is no key to speak of...

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/HomeKitch.jpg]

On the right, a set of mugs and different view of the kitchen.  Mugs are a good thing to have when  you're a tea drinker.  Which I'm re-training my self to be.  I've now been coffee free for 5 or 6 days.  No headaches or shakes.  I'm proud of myself.  Now I'm just praying that being on pager doesn't induce me to drink my fill once more this week.

You may notice that most of my pictures are taken without the use of a flash.  I know that most pictures turn out sharper with the use of a flash, as with the one on the right, I prefer not to use it if I can avoid it.  Natural light.  That, I like. :-)  So, I suppose I should part ways with you all for the evening.  I'm tired, and need my sleep.  A sleep I hope to be at least 8 hours, but know full well there are no guarantees.

May you all walk among the clouds, and be apart from the clouds at the same time.  This is your time to be.  Take it, and take flight!  Shine.  You've all got it.  Believe me, I've seen it.

Sweet dreams, and Peace,

Shane

[Posted 3/28/2005 at 11:36 PM]

=== Thursday March 24, 2005 ===

I Will See for Miles and Miles and Miles

Well, here's what's what.  I'm taking 2 weeks and 2 days off work starting after next week.

Hopefully, on the 2nd of April to the 20th of April I'll be on a roadtrip across Canada.  From Toronto, ON to Whitehorse, YT.

It's approximately 60 hours of driving time, and is 5359.5 Kilometres.  3329.93 miles for my friends from/in the United States.

I'm looking forward to the trip a great deal.  A friend of mine is starting a job in Whitehorse for at least a year and asked if I wanted to go on a roadtrip.  That's how this began.

I get to see a large expanse of Canada.  Not all of what I want to see, but much of the parts that make up it's whole.  Digital camera is coming with.  As is a video recorder.  As are notebooks and reading material.

So, wow.  Well, I'm not gone for a week yet, so I'll be around.  But had to share.

Peace,

Shane

=== Wednesday March 23, 2005 ===

The Dish Ran Away With the Spoon - Fork Left at Home with Kids
(More at the 6:00 News)

Sometimes it takes something to push you into tomorrow.  It always comes down to choices.  Made and unmade.  So what does it take to make the choice to change your life?  I sometimes write as though I have an unbridled spirit.  But I bridle myself every day with the things that are around me.  Growing up with my Dad's lectures.  He was a lecturer.  Choice was one such lecture, a kind of underlying theme in many lectures.  That there's always a choice.  Inaction is one such choice.  To choose not to choose.

I'm faced with a choice right now.  And a deeper choice depending on the result of the first choice.

All things in time.  A time for all things.

++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Just watch me.

I got nothin'

Not yet, not just yet.

++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Peace,

Shane

=== Monday March 21, 2005 ===

Smile Because You Want To

Lets talk of honest teeth.  Upturned mouths, wicked true grins, and the chasm of glee that is belly laughter.

I like honest mouths just like I like honest eyes.  Not an understated kind of honest that's prim and proper.  I don't mind mischief, or playful honesty.  Honestly.

So smile, I'll smile with you.  We can paint the world a different shade, or uncover it's true shade.

Peace,

Shane

=== Monday March 21, 2005 ===

The Sun is Shining - Like a Crazy Diamond

I'm thinking of going on a detox diet shortly.  Primarily to get myself off the copious ammounts of coffee/caffeine to which my body and mind are addicted.  I'm better than the black coffee I force down my gullet in order to kick-start my mind.  Only now, it's more just to feel 'regular' groggy in the morning rather than 'extra' groggy.  Eating healthy is one thing, but I have a feeling a detox diet is going to be rough.  Just want to get some of the poisons out of my system, and try to eat better foods.  Caffeine in and of itself isn't a horrible thing.  It has many positive affects when taken once and a while.  But let me paint a picture:

There's a coffee machine in our office that takes these 'packets' of coffee.  There are three buttons that affect how much water comes through depending on what kind of packet.  'Coffee' 'Espresso' and 'hot chocolate'.  Now, I have four packets each morning in a 'mega mug' with the button 'espresso' because it concentrates the coffee with less liquid.  So, it ends up almost filling the mug.  That's each workday.  Two years ago, I hated coffee.  Drank tea, but still tried to concentrate the tea as much as I could.  For some reason, I switched to coffee and am as addicted as addicted can be.

The sun is out today.  I feel alive today.  Today is a good day.

++++

It's a mobius strip.  It has to be.

++++

The last time we spoke, it was abrupt and short.  I still wonder where you went and if you're okay.

++++

a dark coffee stain;
a ring around the rosy
life, could be better

++++

I wonder if it matters if I'll be remembered for my writing.  If my writing will be remembered?  That our lives have touched is enough.  That our paths have crossed.  That we remember each other is enough.  And not a memory of names, but a memory of meanings.  Our names don't give us meaning, we give meaning to our names.

++++

I want to go to Tibet someday.  Maybe soon, maybe not.  Anyone want to go to Tibet with me?  Mountain air, and lofty ideals.  Pun most definately intended.  But seriously.  Lets go.  I miss mountain tops as much as I miss the ocean.

++++

Gotta go back to work.  This lunch is not enough.

Peace,

Shane

=== Monday March 21, 2005 ===

Life, and Life, and Life - Spring is Near to Here

I feel almost like I'm back.  I mean, present.  Almost like I'm fully present in my life once more.  Though not all my blood test results are back what the doctor could tell me was that my cholesterol was good, my liver was good, my blood pressure and blood sugar levels were also good.  And though the thoughts of the rest of my results kind of hang over me for three more weeks, soon I'll know the full truth.  For now though, I'm fairly more present than I have been off and on for quite some time.

I recently bought the series on DVD called 'Kingdom Hospital'.  A series written based on another series called 'The Kingdom' but by Stephen King largely.  I know not everyone agrees with me when I say King is an excellent writer.  Some people agree, and some do not.  For my own thought on his writing, it's the characters that get me.  His stories are not always the most ingenious, but I wholeheartedly believe that his characterizations are.  And they bring even regular stories to life in ways that other people cannot.  You fall into the shoes of the characters he writes about.

Many of you may be surprised to know that he wrote 'The Shawshank Redemption'.  At least, many people I've mentioned that to have been surprised.  Especially the ones that don't really like King to begin with.  But enough Idol nattering.  I enjoy his characters and the way he brings them to life.  I find myself often relating to that part of myself.  The one that remembers things.  Because I find the way I see him bringing characters to life is by making sure we know they're human.  As human as humans can be.  Unintentional heroes, half-victories, and total failures.

All I'm saying is, don't let your view of King stop at 'Pet Cemetery' or 'Tommyknockers'.

+++++++++++++++++++++++

Your eyes tell me something deep resides within you.  A well of courage, knowledge, love, and strength.  You reside beneath the surface of yourself where you think none can find you fully.  Perhaps they cannot, but don't think that you're as hidden as you believe.  When you're hiding in the dark, your light shines even brighter.  And that, my friend, makes it very hard for you to hide there.  Just because you sometimes close your eyes doesn't mean the world disappears.

So tell me, why do you section yourself into pieces and live only a part at a time?  Do you find it safer that way?  If only a part of you breaks, there'll be more left to work with?  But it's like gambling.  Truly.  Bet with a dollar chip and you get the odds.  5 - 1 gives you five.  If you bet with a 10 dollar chip, you get fifty back.  You get what you risk.  And we truly have nothing at all to lose, and everything to gain.  Don't you think?  We're getting so much closer.

And when you feel rage, to whom do you rage?  Do you rage at hypocracy?  Lethargy of spirit?  Fanaticism?  Love lost, love scorned?  Do you rage because it's something more than nothing?  Do you rage because apathy is worse?  We are connected, you and I.  You rage, I feel it.  When you act on that rage, the guilt is mine to share.  I think that's what I believe.  Oh, we're not responsible for other's actions?  No, perhaps not, but I feel guilty all the same.  If only this, if only that.  One word said, one tear shed.

My guilt is that for all my trying to BE connected to you, I'm not in your shoes.  That is my guilt.  That we stand apart, when we should stand together.  Behind my eyes I know the truth.  As your eyes shout it, so do my own.  I reside beneath the surface of myself.  But I think, one day, you will find me fully.

++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Hope everyone enjoyed their weekend.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 3/21/2005 at 12:0 AM]

=== Monday March 14, 2005 ===

Home is Where There's a Coffee Time Across the Street

So, I've moved in to my new place.  Pictures eventually.  It's a very picture worthy interior.  Old house, good vibes.  Reminds me of a kind of home that I've been away from for too long.  Just a feeling of 'good'.

I just ordered my internet so I should have it sometime this week.  Hopefully tomorrow, but sometime nonetheless.

I also had my physical.  Results this Friday from blood tests.

I'm treating this as if it has the power to bring me peace at last from inner struggles, but the truth is, whatever comes of bloodwork, it is what it is.  Inner peace will have to come from something other than a piece of paper.

There's a coffee time across the street.  24 hours a day, it's open.  What can I say?  It appeals to my insomniac/writer side a great deal. (Also to the side that likes coffee).

Hope all of you are doing well.  I've been playing Sims 2 for the past two nights since my internet is down and out.  I always enjoyed the 'sim' type games.  From the first one I ever played 'Sim Earth' to all of Sid Meyer's creations.  Railroad Tycoon (The original) was another favourite.  Something about looking down on a simulated creation.  Something you created.  In one of my 'Sim Earth' creations, insects became the sentient species of the planet.  They went all the way to exodus, when they started leaving the planet in ships.

In any event, when the Sims first came out, I enjoyed the mix of building buildings.  I like the act of creating.  Anything.

Well, I'm off to work again.

Peace,

Shane

=== Wednesday March 9, 2005 ===

Sanity, Sanitary, Stationary, Salutationary, Stultiloquent

It occurs to me, occurred to me, that my mind has changed fairly
radically in the last few months.  I feel all 'through the looking
glass' at life.

I feel a Cheshire grin.  My mouth a dimple edged canyon.  Come what may.

Come what may.

I've been hard to surprise in my life.  So it's the surprises in
life, the ones that really do surprise me, that I love so much
more.  All life is beautiful, but there's nothing more beautiful
than something that you didn't see coming.  It's so random, a roll
of the dice.

Maybe it's because I have an imagination, and play out even odd
possibilities in my mind.  It means I can say 'I half expected
that' when things do happen.  But friends, I love surprises.
To feel utterly and completely bushwhacked by anything is something I
experience in the positive sense.  Because truly, the same can be
said for the horrible things that can sometimes sideline you.

But enough about finite math and creative minds, enough about me.
I'm going to let my words take me away before I find my way to my
pillow and my ceiling fan, and my deep slumber.

+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

I am convinced that eyes should never be missed when talking to
someone.  I've spent my life to this point looking at the mouths
of people when I talk with them.  Partly because I read lips due
to my not being able to hear every single word very well.  Partly
because I feel less threatened if I'm not looking someone in the
eyes.  I find myself more and more these days looking people in
the eyes when I'm talking to them.  I think I like it.
Things are taking root.

===

Three days before moving and I'm still not packed.  It takes
time.  It'll take me an evening.  But a very full and
complete evening.  And I fear that evening will be Friday.
But it's a thrill.  Like those toys that you keep opening up and
they each have a smaller version of themselves within.  Until you
have 9 of these figures all in a row... except the opposite of
that.  Putting them all together again.  That's what I love
about packing.  It's my life.  It's me in boxes, la bled and
mislabeled.  'Stuff' in one, or 'Misc.' in another.  'Junk
drawer contents' perhaps in another.  But they're all junk drawers
in my room.  They're all things with meaning, but to me.

I used to have some magnetic poetry, and it still has meaning for me,
but the only word that I still have is passion.  And passion
remains.  I wish you saw what I saw.  Why can't people see
their own glowing?  Why can't they see their own wings?  I
see it so often.  One person or another feeling like they're
nothing.  Like they're lower than dirt.  That they are
talent less, worthless, and hopeless.  And don't you doubt for a
moment that they didn't have outrageous talent.  In conversation,
in mind, in art, in word or deed, in emotion or hope.  Talent
unbounded by anything save what they had gotten into their heads about
themselves.  Bars.

I think it's hard to understand or accept sometimes.  That we're
all worth so damn much.  We change reality by our existence.
By our breath.  We change reality by our very perception of
it.  In fact, reality is ours to wield.  Our own!  If
you were not here to perceive it, the world would not exist.  And
perhaps we wouldn't exist as we do if there was nothing to
perceive.  So which came first?  The forest or the trees in
the forest?  It's a kind of paradox.  Except it doesn't have
to be.

Something that has always existed, that doesn't have to have a
beginning, or a set end, that doesn't have to have a 'first', it just
has to have an 'is'.

And this is, my friends, this is.  It's there all around us
because we're here expecting it to be there. (There is no spoon).

We are all creative geniuses.  By our will and action we ripple
out into the world and enact change.  We create.  You cannot
tell me that you do not matter, because the minute you utter such
words, you already matter more than you ever thought you did.  In
that instant you matter to me more than you'll ever know, or perhaps
believe.

You can hurt me with action, inaction, cutting words, misunderstanding,
or a burning hate of all I may represent.  But you can't hurt the
fact that I love you all the same.  And you can't change the truth
of that no matter how you try.

We share the air, you and I, our paths are crossed you and I, our paths
our one, as is our from and to.  We wear different faces, but you
know me as well as I know you.  Beneath the skin, and underneath
the soul.  Follow the line and you can't miss the centre.

And that fact terrifies me as much as thrills me.  Because I have a human mind.  And so do you.

=====

I remember it all.  I can tell you where I was when Mars looked
down from above, red and hopeful.  Friendship and heartbreak soon
after.

I can tell you the expression on your face that day I said and did
things that caused pain beyond any I ever thought I would ever
inflict.  Out of fear, and weakness.

I can tell you the way the grass felt under my feet in those fields of my youth when unicorns were real, and I could fly.

I can tell you about the way the bird lay on the cement moving, though
the bird itself wasn't moving save for what was moving inside of
it.  I can tell you of the horror of that realization.

I can tell you of pillows and tears.  Me, yes.  They're not
just for yawns after 'emotional' flicks in dark theatres where nobody
can see.  You keep a tear inside that is meant to be spent into
the world, and you begin to rupture something inside of yourself.
I can tell you the truth of that as surely as I can tell you I learned
that lesson well.  If you must keep things inside, even for just a
while, let them out as soon as you can.  At a wall for anger, or a
pillow for sorrow, a friend for laughter, and a friend for tears
too.  A bottled tear is a small silent death of something worth
feeling.

Emotion is life as surely as a pinprick and blood is life.  Don't
be so quick to stifle half of yourself away.  You can't really
fly with only one wing.

I can tell you that I'm going to bed now because I find myself saying
more and more that I don't mean to be preachy, and that I'm talking as
much to myself as to anyone reading.  The fact of the matter is
though, that there are some people I'd love to tell these things
to.  Basically anybody that would need to hear these words.

The fact TRULY is, anything you feel inside your head, heart,
body.  Anything at all, is something that someone else is either
feeling or thinking somewhere else in the world.  It's what you do
with it that counts.  You're not stupid for thinking the thoughts
you do, or weak for feeling the emotions you do.

My rant, self declaration, sleepytime synopsis, is now over.  I wish you sweet dreams and pleasant awakenings.

As always,

Shane

[Posted 3/9/2005 at 12:1 AM]

=== Monday March 7, 2005 ===

Moongodess at the River's edge

Moongodess at the River's edge

that flows from life to distand lands

through which caverns can be scaled

with suns that bleach the once dark sands.

Hear now the voice of fisherfolk,

invoke your name in honest prayer,

to make their take just one more day,

And end at shore, beneath you there.

+++

Shane Fera

Incomplete, as ever, but I'm tired and the fisherfolk really
must find their port of call before the moon fades to black for a few
days.  Peace to you all,

Shane

=== Sunday March 6, 2005 ===

Don't count your chickens before they've hatched, but don't discount them either...
=============================================================

The future is like the candy dish you may have looked forward to at a relative's place when you were a child.  Sometimes there would be the best candy in the world in that dish, and sometimes there would be these stale jube-jubes from a couple of visits ago that really shouldn't be there anymore.  It's one massive candy dish, and I'm about to lift the lid on the future for another year.

I'm moving this Saturday from one place to another in Toronto.  This Saturday is the beginning of my next year in a way.  A year in a house with a dear friend while finding my salt, and testing my mettle in writing, love, and the 'near downtown' experience.  I spent the first half of my life thinking.  I may very well spend the next half of my life doing.  There's just lots of stuff that needs doing.  Books to be written (though writing ABOUT them doesn't help in the writing OF them), people to be met, and the future love of my life to be found.  Seems like a small list, but it's a start.

I'm not voicing a complaint here or anything, just stating facts about how the last couple of years of my life have gone.  They've gone pretty damn well.  I've got my career on track really, and though I shudder to call my current job my career, it's a place for now that's providing me money for talking to people on the phone and being a positive force in the workplace.  I mean, fu ck.  How can you beat that?  The thing of it is though, in my last two years of transition I've not been focusing much on the meeting of 'new' people, nor in the pursuit of love and my ultimate happiness.

Ultimate happiness you ask?  Yes.  And it's strange to even talk about pursuing something that has an undetermined source, but I wouldn't mind finding that thing that just takes me there.  My bliss.  My bliss isn't really writing.  That's a confession.  My bliss is people.  My bliss is people's emotions and thoughts.  Their individuality.  But in all the sea of individuality, there's one I desire.  One that must call out to me, or so I hope.  The search for the spark, in eyes and action.  In lips and passion.  The full meaning, and all of them, of the word passion.  For each other and the lives we may lead.

Lofty goals?  Maybe.  My wax has always been just a little bit of altitude away from melting completely off my wings; but if you don't fly higher than maybe is safe, how can you see the distance that's open to you?

So hey, help a guy with lofty goals out here.  If you find the girl of my dreams could you let her know where to find me?  I kinda woke up before I got her number.

Thanks, and peace,

Shane

[Posted 3/6/2005 at 10:8 PM]

=== Thursday April 28, 2005 ===

Riddles

If you like riddles, solving riddles, trivia I think, or abstract connectedness, just follow me:

http://ourcolony.net/ will get you to the front page.

Enter 'play' into the empty text box, then click on the ant.

=== Tuesday April 26, 2005 ===

The Stigma

No, not the stigmata, the stigma.  This post kind of came to me while I was crushed in between two others on the bus to work this morning.  It always seemed to me that there was some kind of unwritten rule about the bus.  That if along the seats that go lengthwise through the back of the bus there was a single open seat between to full seats, that said empty seat should remain empty.  I guess it always seemed like it was an unwritten rule because I'd always see the single empty seats scattered through the back of the bus with people still standing in the aisle.

Well, this morning I broke this unwritten rule and sat between two people in the empty seat that was calling to me.  I can't be sure, because I make a point not to look anyone in the eye on the bus (another unwritten rule, though if you do catch someone's gaze you either have to look away right away, or keep looking at them until they look away).  So, I can't be sure, but I'm fairly certain all eyes fell on me instantly.  I could almost hear their unuttered gasps of incredulity and horror.

I then proceeded to close my eyes until my stop.  Half-asleep, but also aware that given half the chance they'd all brand me with some kind of scarlet letter and throw me off the bus.  I close my eyes most days on the bus because it's a hell of a lot better than playing eye avoidence, or glancing up at the posters telling people how wonderful the transit system is or how some disease is a common thing, and that those who have it shouldn't feel helpless because calling some number would put them in touch with the right doctors...

So now I'm wondering how I'll face those people tomorrow.  Because lets face it, when you ride a certain bus to work, it usually has many of the same people on it day in and day out.  I carry with me a stigma now.  The one who dared sit where no others had sat before.  I think I can do it.  I think I can make it through tomorrow, and the next day.  I'll wear my stigma proudly, but God help anyone who dares sit in any empty seat beside me!

:-)

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 4/26/2005 at 10:0 AM]
