=== Friday April 22, 2005 ===

[IMAGE: http://xeb.xanga.com/ada85153d85325548864/z4776364.jpg]All Roads Lead to Home

It's a matter of course that after a journey, you find yourself home.  It's another matter of course that the home we end up in isn't ever the home we left.  We can't embark on any journey with any certainty as to what the home will be like at the end.  But we journey all the same.  I understand that there are many people who read my last couple of posts both in the Xanga community and outside of the Xanga community.  We all live our lives in so many pieces.  In the hearts and thoughts of people who know us as we walk down our paths in life.  And that's partly how we live on after we're gone from this beautiful place.  In the hearts and souls of those who are left to remember.

I have some pictures I'm going to post and I'm not certain of whether I'll write about absolutely everything right now, but I wanted to show some of the Country in which I live, and that I love.  I must admit, after this adventure I love mountains almost as much as I love the ocean.

[IMAGE: http://x6c.xanga.com/5f482a51462325549058/z4776471.jpg]

The mountain air, the crisp sky and brilliant sun above.  Isolated in the Rockies along the Alaska Highway.  I may have survived the Alaska Highway, but a piece of me now rests with those lofty peaks and rolling rivers that nestle in many of the valleys.

[IMAGE: http://x16.xanga.com/df081b47534315549201/z4776550.jpg]

[IMAGE: http://x99.xanga.com/25783651546305549231/z4776568.jpg]

[IMAGE: http://x9a.xanga.com/ac085052567325549275/z4776593.jpg]

I also stopped in Dawson Creek.  Apparently the show that was a smash hit (though I've never actually seen it) is based on real life stories from this sleepy Alberta town, in which the Alaska Highway begins.  Well, at least I'm trying to convince everyone that the show is based on a Canadian town.

The Prairies were nice.  Northern Ontario was beautiful, but the great Canadian Grain Belt was nice as well.  Faster driving, farther horizon, longer shadows.

And the grain elevator was neat to see.  Though there were many, many, many along the way.  And I'm pretty sure they exist in Ontario as well, but seeing them against the backdrop of fields larger than I've ever seen in one place, that's the ticket.

[IMAGE: http://x84.xanga.com/d9d87047734345549479/z4776696.jpg]

Caribou. I also got to see Caribou which I've never seen before.  They seem to look like a cross between deer and moose, though I've never seen a moose up close.  Unfortunately there weren't any wandering the highways during the day.  These particular caribou had attempted to cross the road behind us only to come face to face with some cars that scared them back to their more-comfortable riverbed.

Personaly, I'd probably enjoy walking along a riverbed much more than a road myself.  Though I suppose it would have taken substantially longer to walk to Whitehorse.  Which was a very beautiful town also.  Smaller than my hometown of Georgetown in population, it made up for it with it's tranquility.  At least, in someplaces.

I wandered out one night to take a look at the northern lights which I've never seen, only to come face to face with the horrible realization that they weren't out.  So in my wandering I found myself in a park-area which I quickly found out was a grave-yard.  Now in most circumstances, finding myself walking through a park rather than a graveyard would have entirely creeped me out.  The fact was, with a half-moon above, the stars brilliant in the sky, and the air cool but not cold I just had to keep walking.

I think I love tranquility as much as I love the hum of the city.  I don't know if I'll ever be able to really decide, but I'll keep trying both out all the days of my life I think.  Hermit on, hermit off.  I think I can do both with some success.  I think I'd rather experience more of everything rather than become an expert of any one thing.

I think life is beautiful.

So I leave you with these pictures, thoughts, and an 'I'm Back' and should have internet from my room at home again soon.  Right now I'm working on setting up a wireless network so I'm kind of 'between' things right now.

Adieu for now,

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 4/22/2005 at 2:37 PM]

=== Thursday April 7, 2005 ===

From Above, The World is Still a Beautiful Place

So far I'm in Saskatoon, Saskatchewan.  We're headed to Edmonton tomorrow, in Alberta.  But what I'm writing about today is some news I received while I was in Manitoba.  I wrote a piece a while ago, about a year ago, about my Grandmother's house.  I'm going to be re-posting it shortly so that it will appear just below this entry.  I never ended up continuing with my journey through the house, or even into the house.  I feel that I should write about it now.  My grandmother passed away on Wednesday morning and as she looks over my shoulder, I want to finish what I started last year.

The much beloved house written about in the post below contains more than it's white-siding outside.  It contains more than a driveway that fills with water in the back, and a tree-stump that used to house a tree.  It contains many rooms, built piece by piece by it's owners to house themselves, their children, and the memories that they would create.  I wanted to have pictures with this post as I took some last year during my week visit, however, as I'm away from Ontario at the moment the pictures will be entered into this later.

The first thing you notice when you enter the house is the sense of coming home that it instills I think in anyone that has ever visited it's walls.  A sense of peace, welcome, and love.  The next thing you might notice (as you hit your head on it) is an antique telephone just next to the entranceway.  A phone I used to revel in turning the handle of, since it rings it's bell as  you turn the handle.  As you bend over to pick the piece of the phone that always falls off when your head knocks it, you may notice two statue-heads hung on the wall of sailors.  The intricacy of the carving, and the detail, make you want a closer look.

In front of the doorway is a narrow stairway leading up to the upstairs bathroom, and it's two bedrooms.  To the left of the stairs is the kitchen, a back room, and to the left of that, the living room.  As your head pans from the stairs to the kitchen, to the living room, you see the fixture of the house sitting in her chair watching her soaps.  At least, you'd see her there during those certain times of the day that her soaps air.  Of course, beyond the soaps I remember one show that always reminds  me of Grandma.  The price is right.  We'd often sit in her visits to us in the south, or my visits north, in front of the TV guessing prices on American merchandise.

My Grandmother is as much a fixture of that house as the walls themselves.  A house she saw rise from the ground and a house in which she came to rest as my Grandfather did many years before.  I can remember the kitchen with fondness.  For a number of reasons.  Besides the living-room which was often a destination, the kitchen was the heart of the house.  A place where we'd all sit around the table talking, as it also adjoined to the back room.  (The back room used to be a living room of sorts.  It used to be where I remember us kids hanging out while the adults talked in the kitchen or living room.).

(I apologize for the scattered nature of this writing, there are so many memories and I want to share as many as I can.  I may re-work the words another time.  Just not right now.)

In a visit I had with my grandmother when I was still in grade school, I remember her teaching me a game called 'Spite and Malice'.  We played with just two, and though that was lots of fun we also went to visit my Uncle Bob and his family at his cottage\home.  Playing spite and malice with as many people as we did certainly spiced up the game.  And my grandmother definitely enjoyed the game!

Her name is Anita Fera.  She had patience, and a stubborn streak to go hand in hand with that patience.  Of course, raising 6 kids all 4 years apart I believe, gives you both the patience and the stubbornness.  She loved and was loved by many.  She went through joys and hardships, and though the kitchen might have seemed to be the heart of the house it's my Grandmother that remains the heart of that house to me.

One time in a visit I remember being curious about everything.  Actually, I often had questions she'd happily answer as she remembered the past.  Her childhood growing up in a house on a hill.  The way the house grew, the way my Grandfather was. Recently it was her asking questions about what they were talking about Mars, and what all the fuss was about.  I remember feeling happy that I could explain something for her and answer one of her questions as she had answered so many of my own growing up.

She told me a story about a train-ride she had.  Her first (and last I think she said) train ride that my Grandfather took her on.  From a station that no longer exists in Coniston where she lives, to the very close city of Sudbury.  Hearing the story brought a smile to my face.  How much she'd been through.

There are so many things I want to write about my Grandmother, my memories seem to be boundless when I go over them.  Her puttering around the kitchen always wanting to make sure you were fed.  Long after you were already full.  I think she wanted to help the starving of the world but re-associated that 'wanting to help the starving' to feeding everyone who came inside her front doors.  And frankly, it was always okay with me.  I remember her lemon meringue pie.  Her butterscotch pie.  Her meatballs, and pasta.

She left a legacy behind.  Her family, their families, and their families families.  And each of us has our memories of her in our hearts.  Each of us has our stories to tell, and our love to share.  She raised 6 hard-headed, determined, intelligent, loving, family oriented children.  And each of them has gone through their life doing the same where they could.  For their immediate family, or their extended family.  In this she has left herself behind in each of us who's lives she has touched.  She loved us all as much as any one person can love any other.  Unconditionally, and eternally.

I wish my thoughts would come more lucidly as I write this.  There's so much more I'd love to share.  She was a special lady, one who has touched my life more than I could ever write in words.  She's up above now, and all I can do is continue in my life what she inspired in others.  To live and love those people in our lives.  Because life comes and goes, but the love we share carries on through those we love.

I wish you all peace and love,

Shane Fera

[Posted 4/7/2005 at 11:29 PM]

=== Thursday April 7, 2005 ===

So Many Beginnings

There are so many places I can begin the stories I'm about to tell you.  There are so many places to start sharing my memories, but I'm going to pick one place in particular.  A view that always meant we were 'there' when I was growing up.  A view that always meant the long trip from Brampton to Coniston was over.  (And believe me, a four and a half hour drive is torture when you're that young.  Every minute seems like a decade.)  So, we begin with the lane.  I still don't really know if it has a name.  I don't think it's ever been a question I've asked,  but to me it's always been 'the lane'.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/lane1.jpg]

It's a small gravel road that leads behind the yards of houses that face the other direction.   A back lane, but the path to reach the driveway of my Grandmother's house.  From this view, you can see the entrance, and a white house on the left corner.  That house used to be a two storey (maybe three) building that used to contain many different things in it's life.  My favourite being a candy shop for a short time.  At least, short enough for me to have gone in that particular shop only once before it most likely relocated or just plain closed up.  And I imagine it didn't just sell candy, but when you're young and have a dollar in your hand, what else is there in a convenience shop?

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/lane2.jpg]On the right you can see farther down the lane.  Garbage collection picks up from the back of the houses.  Hide and seek included the entire lane, and the yards attached.  Out of bounds were the main roads that frame the lane and the houses.  I absolutely loved to play hide and seek when I was younger.  And then 'manhunt' when I was older.  But I'm sure we all knew it was just hide-and-seek with a 'cooler' name.  There's nothing quite so satisfying as finding someone who thought they could outsmart you with their hiding spot.  And there's the even better feeling of never being found during a game.  Home Free.

In the yard next to my Grandmother's used to live a man who I could never make up my mind about.  Sometimes he seemed mean, and others very kind.  He always reminded me of the man from 'The Old Man and the Sea".  Quintino.  He had a parrot that lived in his garage.  He had a beautiful garden.  And he had a a brick house.  I was only ever in his garage once to see the parot.  I don't remember if I was scared of the bird, but I think he died while we were living in Australia.  So, my memories of him and that parrot are from when I was 7 and younger.

[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/lane3.jpg]That is the shed that exists behind my Grandmother's house.  The pot you see sitting in the corner of the yard is resting on the stump of where my favourite tree in the whole world used to sit.  It's my favourite tree, I think, because of the wonderful tree-smell that used to come off it in the fall and spring.  I'm not certain what kind of tree it was either, except that whenever I smell that smell in the fall or spring, I'm back in this yard, and I'm 6 again.  And I can hear the children of coniston playing in the yards around.  And I can hear the person who's 'it' counting off by the trunk.  I have a feeling, though not a solid memory, that the tree was often home-free.

The shed itself was a mystery to me for a long time.  The door was hard to open.  It still is, as the railway tracks are one street over... and every time a train goes by the ground shakes.  Needless to say, the shed leans a little bit, and the door frame isn't a perfect recangle anymore.

Once, there were a bunch of cats that were holed up under the barn.  I don't know if they were someone's who had a litter, or just wild cats.  (Probably not wild, because I wasn't afraid of them.)  And since I always had a fascination with cats, I stalked them around when they would come out into the next-door neighbour's yard.  There used to be a fence where that little trelliswork fence used to be.  A great big 5 foot fence that used to tower over our tiny heads.  But that we could climb over easilly at a certain spot.[IMAGE: http://i.xanga.com/Stultiloquent/thehouse.jpg]

And finally, the house.  In this picture, we're facing it from the back, and the shed from the previous picture is positioned to the left of me, taking the picture.  You can see the cement steps to the back porch, from which Grandma would hang her laundry to dry.  You can see a little brown rectangle on the left side of the house.  That's a door that opens and there's a line that runs from it out to the shed.  The laundry line.  (And a pefect sized door for a 6 year old to climb through and into the house if they were trying to be sneaky.)

In this picture, you can see my aunt Terry at the middle-right of the picture.  She's as much a fixture in my memories as the house.  She's my Grandma's sister in law, I believe.  You see, where most of the houses on the street have one house, and a yard in the back.  This lot has two houses.  My Grandma's built in the back, from the ground up as I"ll explain later, and in the front, the house that used to belong to my Grandmother's Mother-in-Law.  The cement in the back, where the cars would usually park, always used to fill up with water when it rained.  Practically a lake, right there in the backyard.  And that back porch?  Always the place my Grandma would wave from when we left after our trips.  We'd see her in that back window, waving away.

And for now, I'm going to leave it at that.  There's still a few things to talk about in the yard itself, but it's sleepy-by time for Shane.

Goodnight, and Peace,

Shane

[Posted 4/7/2005 at 11:25 PM]

=== Sunday April 3, 2005 ===

And Away I Go

So, today I'm off to the great wide west, and then the great white
north.  Whitehorse here I come.  Northern lights, here I
come.  Actual stars in the night sky, here I come.  64+ hours
of in-car time, here I come.  Of course, that'll be broken up in
chunks of 8 or 10 hour trips.  With stopovers in Edmonton,
Winipeg, and possibly anything else that catches our eye in the great
flat that is the expanse  between Ontario and Western Canada.

Peace, everyone, be good whie I'm gone.  Hopefully I'll
have stories of the road to tell you all when I get back.  Of the
country I love to live in.

Your northern neighbour (for those readers from the U.S.A),

Shane

the soundtrack of my life, or so to speak
and i will dance or not while listening to the beat
and watching life around me live

livelier than my usual tuesday night

a night like any other

a Toronto tuesday night

=== Monday May 30, 2005 ===

i betray myself

never could decide upon a time or place
pick one to be your everything
just one to be your all
a single vision with unity?

i frolicked in those fields, where everything made sense because nothing made sense
the bees were out to get us, the teachers too
and the girl who had a prison for a home inside her head

and still i wonder what is real in all of this
this utopia of sense and nonsense
of solid fantasy, moulded by desire en-masse

i picked my truth from age of seven,
handpicked amongs the bleeding hearts that hedged that yard
and tyrants in the classroom twisting truths and stealing lies

no lies to call their own, she was a witch I'm sure
long past the time where teaching felt good
and took her spite upon us all, in memory at leat

you wanted me, you asked for me,
i'll give you piece by piece, my offering
i can offer naught but myself
and you can have it all

i am memory incarnate, action at instant, time and space,
you haven't seen or heard the least of what floats around my room
this late at night when moonlight filters through the reaching trees

so you can have it all, each word in sequence and out of too,
i never liked the lines to stay within, that is not passion; rules
that is not momentary brilliance keeping well within your bounds

if you could see what i see but for a moment how i see

if if if, perhaps we'd get along well after all

where filtered moonbeams are enough to sooth the soul
and calm a rustled mind to sleep

but not that deep, not yet, not ever if i had my way

+++

Shane

=== Friday May 27, 2005 ===

Geopolitical, Sociological, Nonsensical, Whimsical me.

+++

S is my favourite letter in the alphabet I think.  It's soft, sensual, passionate, sssmoooth.  I mean, there's just something about the letter S that makes everything alright in the world.  I'm not even joking.  Thin on material you ask?  No, not really.  But it's that time of the morning/night where I just write what's on the tip of my mind so I don't have to go digging through the murk and mire of a tired yet restless mind.

+++

He noticed her from across the room, not because her beauty was a silent wave that swept through the party, but because her beauty held with it a defiance.  She wore little makeup, clothes that fit well but showed little, and an expression that dared conversation.  He noticed her because she didn't want to be noticed.  The music pulsed, the crowd shifted, and his line of vision to her closed.  He had marked her face, her eyes, and knew that she was the only one in the room that would captivate him.

+++

Some fear is about not having control of a situation.  But that is the kind of fear that has no point except to make matters worse.  If there is not a way to have control of a situation, all that can be done is ride the situation out as best as you can.  We may not be able to always control which way the wind blows, but we can control ourselves to either meet it head on, or face away.  And at least for me, I've always loved to meet wind head on.  It's one of two things that change my energy when it's present around me.  The first is the full moon, the second is the wind.  A grey-green blustery day sparks me to life like nothing else.  The possibility of storming, with the warm air in the wind conflicting with the chill stationary air.  Wind is a dance between opposites.  And it's contrast like that I love so much.

+++

I really think I'm heading to bed now.  It's 1:15 and I'm kaput.  My body's screaming for more than 6 hours of sleep, and I'm screaming for just a few more hours in the day.  30 would be fine.  Maybe 32.  More time to be awake, and more time to dream at night.  Now that would be perfection, at least from my present point of view.  And it's always about point of view.  It's how the world works really.  We've all got them, and they're all absolutely and utterly different.  My blue is different than your blue.  Your red is different from my own.

It's invigorating.  The mystery is starting to invigorate me again.  It comes in waves, and I'm starting to learn how to bodysurf.

Peace,

Shane

=== Monday May 23, 2005 ===

Not Inured to your Absence

Would that I could blink, and you'd be there,
Deep eyes, fast smile, and your midnight hair,
Laughing at the storm of fleeting lives,
Apart from them, and all the world's contrives.

+++

apart, now I stand
a discordant storm within
Harmony's echo

+++

That I could freeze time such, to view a life,
Unlived now lived in parallel to this,
To recognize the wrong and end the strife,
Right all the wrongs, redo all that I miss.

+++

Your lips, your lips, that I have kissed.
Beneath the moon, such tender bliss.
Remarking on the earth a while,
on all of love and nature's smile.
We talked of future, present, past,
of simple life and upper class;
and when the moon sank low that morn,
I swore you were why I was born.
With passion's fire clasped in my heart,
You'd be my end, as well as start.
I knew this from my soul to feet,
I knew it all till night's retreat.
How could I know when morning came,
That time's swift passage would be to blame.
Though life is in a moment spent, and hearts thrown in the fire fast
We learn that change remains present, and with such change a fonder past.

+++

My heart sleeps on the floor because I dare not bring it to an empty bed.  Where memories exist with such ferocious vividness as to bring me to that place where long ago is now.  We held hands all night, counting our heartbeats together.

Memories are so much more perfect than the time actually spanned.  Imperfection fades, and choices made are blurred.  I love the moment, and I'll bring it back again.  Where eternity is lived in shallow breaths, anxious passion and naked souls.  Bathed in moonlight, and a summer breeze.

+++

Would that I could blink and you'd be there.
A distant memory with midnight hair.

+++

Shane

[Posted 5/23/2005 at 4:8 PM]

=== Thursday May 19, 2005 ===

The Burning Man - II

I'm back.  There wasn't a group specifically for this event, so I have created a weblog group "The Burning man".  I don't know what kind of interest the community here has in this event.  My search of Xanga through the Xangan front page brought up some dated entries from last year.  Though I know, know, know, that many of you are interested in such things.  In the people, the summer solstice, the art.  (And some of you may have that 'special' relationship with the fire part of the whole thing as well.  Which is fine!  I seriously doubt it's about 'judging' at such an event.).

It's only May.  It's only may and I know it's going to be on my mind until I go.  This year's theme is "Psyche: the Conscious, the Subconscious and the Unconscious".  I don't think I could have picked a more fitting year to make a first attendance.  I'm not the greatest 'artist' as far as visual art is concerned, but I'm going to try to think of a creative way to represent the theme in what I can do with a pen and paper.

I know I sound like a kid in a candy store, but you know what?  I am that excited.  I don't know what next year will bring, or the year after.  Hell, I don't know what tomorrow will bring.  But I know that life's too short to sweat reasons why not to do things.  The desert heat is one thing I fear in a sense.  I dislike heat.  The cold nights of the desert are something I'm looking forward to.  But the daytime heat.  Hell, I like contrast though.  Maybe my like of contrast will override my dislike of heat.  It'll be a dry heat at the very least, which is something we don't get around here.  It's wet heat that you can wring out at the end of the day.  Having a lake nearby will do that to a weather zone.

I really am going to bed now.  I feel silly expressing the slight euphoria I'm going through right now as far as enery is concerned.  Those that know me personally know that I am usually a reserved person.  At least, reserved in the 'excited' range of emotion.

The world is round.  Roll with it.

Sweet dreams,

Shane

=== Wednesday May 18, 2005 ===

Burning Man

So, this year I guess I'm being adventurous.  I'm now settling in to the planning of my trip in September to the Burning Man.  If you haven't heard of it, this handy website offers a plethora of information.  It seems exactly my speed with it's mix of absolutely anything.  "An experiment in temporary community" is kind of what it's considered.  It's a gathering of people on a dried out lake-bed outside of Vegas.  Hot days, cold nights, stars above, and a community of a mix of 'Hippies, Wierdos, Normals, Abnormals, Artists, Writers, Yuppies, Guppies.... and well, anyone at all I think.

I'm excited about this adventure.  About the people that I'll meet, and the living art I'll experience and be a part of.  If this goes well, I have a feeling I may go again next year.  I've never been and really don't have any preconceived notion of how it will be.  Actually, I think I'm going to see if theres a Blogring for this event because it would definately be interesting to see if 'anyone I don't know' is going.

Peace, be well, and all that jazz,

Shane

=== Sunday May 15, 2005 ===

The Weekend Ramble by Shane Fera
(Because writing a single poem every single day is just too much structure for me and possibly... a weekly stream of everything ramble is not.)

[IMAGE: http://xaa.xanga.com/06014061580a41833423/z1766040.jpg]

So.  Seriously.  I'm a person that does not seem to be very consistent.  An expression that has been used by myself (and others) is all talk and no action.  And by this moment's existence, I believe that may be true.  And it's gone past the first stage where I deny it outright.  And it's gone past the second stage where I just don't make any statements whatsoever.  And it's hit the level that it's been for a while now.  Acceptance of a sorts, with the intention to self improve, but by the saying of such intention dooms itself to failure.

Does that make sense?  Probably.  At least, even if the words don't make sense in and of themselves, I'm sure you get their intended meaning.  I always got 'Awkward Sentence' sprawled at least a couple of times on things I'd write for English class.  But I'm certain they always understood my meaning.  'Awkward Sentence' might rather mean 'Too artsy for an Essay'.  Or perhaps 'Conform.  Conform.  Conform.'.  Which brings me to another question.  What is conformity?  And hell, if you're not conforming just to not conform, aren't you conforming with the non-conformists?  Really.  I mean seriously.  it's always confused the hell out of me.

I've met many people that didn't 'conform' and many were just being exactly who they were.  What they wanted without fear or expectation of reaction from others.  Other people were being 'different' just for the sake of being 'different'.  And really, there's nothing wrong with that right?  But it's the same to me as being the same just for the sake of being the same.

Me?  I used to be the kind who tried to fit in but always failed miserably.  Then there was a period where I tried not to fit in, tried to stand out.  Class clown.  Being 'odd'.  Whatnot.  Now I think I'm some kind of hybrid.  Though I imagine most of us fit somewhere between the two extremes.  (What extremes? That's true.  It isn't just fitting in or not fitting in.  You'd have to define normal then, and come up with a better answer than 'whatever the majority is doing.)  Because frankly, the majority of people, us human beings, live on the other side of the planet.

I think I may have strayed somewhere off my point... if I ever had a point.  My latest stage of staying I'll try to self improve, and then inevitably not doing so.
(bear with me here, I'm realizing that I'm just going to ramble.  And I'm sure only a handful will read all the way through.  But that's okay.  This here's for me.  it's just one of those nights.)

I'm trying desperately to figure out what the next stage should be.  In Maslow's Hierarchy of needs I think I'm doing okay.  But really, I think it's a bit more complicated than that.  It goes beyond a building-block look at a human existence.  I'm also trying desperately to swim against the current of my own thoughts.  The mind is a raging river that does not give heed to things like it's own banks, or dams, or any other blockade for that matter.  The fact that I have a mind to swim against is something that I'm thankful for.  That I can appreciate the morning sun, and the evening stars.  That each day I take a breath in, and thank It.  I thank the day.  I thank the moment.  I thank anything and everything behind making that moment come into existence.

I think we have to be tourists in our lives.

I think you know what I mean.  When we're in tourist mode we have a camera handy.  Our eyes are more open.  Our mouths taste things more deeply, our hands feel things more intensely.  Our emotions run high, and we take everything in so completely.  At least, I think that most tourists do.  I think we have to be a tourist in our own lives so that we can learn not to take it all for granted.  That you are reading this right now taking in these words means the difference between here and there.  That  you wake in the morning, to something.  That it is there to greet you and your very conscious mind.  That means something.

I think I'm very tired.  And I think far too much.  It's a vice I'm sure I could do without but pray I will never be without.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 5/15/2005 at 1:58 AM]

=== Monday May 9, 2005 ===

Mom, Mommy, Mother, Mum

On a day like Mother's day when we celebrate one half of the reason why we're here, I guess it's only appropriate to pay tribute to my Mom here online as well.

My Mother is a Taurus.  In fact, her birthday of May 9th often falls on Mother's day itself.  She was born in a small town in Northern Ontario.  I believe her place of birth was while her parents were living at the town of St. Charles.  Born into a French Canadian family, she quickly became bi-lingual as is necessary when most elsewhere in Ontario is largely English speaking.  She was born a fraternal twin.

My Mum is stubborn.  I think it's the Taurus in her.  Or just living with my dad for so long... seeing as his stubbornness comes not from his sign but from his genetics.  I'm unsure yet as to the extent of the 'stubborn' gene into my own genetics from my parents, but I'll leave that to my future wife to point out at such a time I have a wife.

My Mom is loving spiritual, creative, emotional, determined, beautiful, and eager for new things and old things alike.  She raised me in the Catholic traditions, and though I do not follow the Catholic faith it is the foundation of my spirituality from which I sprung.  We used to play Lego, and colour.  That was our thing.  In this way she sparked my creativity and challenged my mind with possibilities.  She also (when I was under 6 years old) went with me to the library to pick out some books on the process of reproduction.  As I imagine I asked the fated question of where I came from.  I remember looking at a picture of an Ovum.  And since the words described it as an egg, I exclaimed "That doesn't look like an egg!".

She rocked me when I was sick.  Often sung me to sleep, and absolutely every Christmas for a time, sang Silent Night to me.

She is my mother.  I love her.  Happy Mother's Day!

Shane

[Posted 5/9/2005 at 12:29 AM]

I didn't see the fates last night as I slumbered as deeply as the London fog is thick.  Pea-soup dreams, but not nearly as tasty or memorable as such.  Just a blink from then till morning.

I fear the picture will throw itself into a digital oblivion from the weight of such a burden, but I'm too tired to care about it's future destination.  For now, I shall carry myself into the bed that waits for me; towards the dream that wait for me as well.  Thought our meeting may not be fated, our meeting certainly was.

May your own paths lead you to your own destinations.  And, may our paths cross again on the morrow.

=== Monday May 2, 2005 ===

Full Moon Withdrawal and Other Symptoms of Life

Is it everything you hoped it would be.  More, to live and breathe where angels cannot tread.  But what from life can bring us to the place we journey to hereafter... before after. Hmm?  I used to think I had all the cards in my hand.  I truly did.  Like absolutely honestly.  Oh, I understood that there were mysteries.  That there were things not yet explained.  But I used to just acknowledge that everything was exactly how I expected it to be.

[IMAGE: http://xbb.xanga.com/bda0447558db56007191/z5065806.jpg]And most of my life it has been.  Exactly how I've expected it to be.  Surprise is something that hasn't played a large part in my life.  Playing chess in your head will do that.  You expect anything, because you've played out possibilities in your head, so you're never surprised.  That's how I felt.  So, to tackle most questions you only need to move a few pieces forward to see the paths.  But to tackle other, deeper questions, one game of chess is not enough.  When the entire chessboard of the mind is not enough, how can you plan the paths?

Now I'm starting to realize, however, that if you expect a lake to be a lake, you're not going to be surprised.  But if you expect a lake to ripple exactly how you picture it in your head, or the loons to bale at the moon in exactly the same way you hear in your mind's eye, then you will be surprised.  It's easy to expect life to be life, and an asshole to be an asshole, or a friend to be a friend.  But zoom in closer.  Your friend is your friend, but someone else's asshole.  It's like the expression 'Beauty is in the eye of the beholder'.  We're all so good at beholding.

Behold you, beholding me.  It's in-fuckin-sanity.  But there are an infinite number of perspectives on any given moment.  It's like some class in high school where they teach that everyone wears masks.  Or, rather, has 'roles' to play.  And play different roles.  A father is a friend is a businessman, is a son.  A woman, is a mother, is a fisherman's wife, is a daughter, is a lover, is an honest woman, and a creep.

Considering that these roles grow and shrink as life goes on there really isn't any place you can stop and say 'I am complete'.  I am whole.  Your roles change.  Change is a common factor.  And people have all sorts of theories on change.  Is change chaotic, planned, somewhere in between.  Is change our collective ID and EGO trying to shape our inner thoughts to reality?

Definitely not sure where my point has come or gone to in all of these words.  Just that I still have the same cards in my hand, but instead of them being the all and only cards there are, there's still about a 20 Deck Shoe of cards waiting to be dealt out.  And reshuffled.  And dealt out again.  Impossible to count.  At least, by me, holding the 8 cards that I hold.

Honestly now, how crazy does all this sound?  Because I realize that my writing takes many forms, and jumps from lucidity to stuff like this from time to time.  And I often wonder to myself, how do you see me?  Those that don't know me but from words.  How do you see this strange person who writes these kinds of things at 2 in the morning?

-

I met the three fates in a dream once.  No, seriously, they were in a classroom teaching baking.  Clotho, Lachesis, and Atropos.  Very kind women, despite the fact that they handle life, life paths, and then death.  I do not remember a word that was said, only that I was given a cookie and they said I'd be back one day.  (Oh, and this dream was much before the Matrix) So please forgive my mind giving my dream that kind of gloss.  I think I should head back tonight, because this writing has raised some more questions I wouldn't mind having answered.

Well, this nut's going to bed.  Sleep, then work, then 5 days of anti-bucolic bliss.  Then 2 days of something other than that.  Rinse, wash, repeat.

Sweet Dreams,

Shane

[Posted 5/2/2005 at 2:11 AM]

=== Sunday June 26, 2005 ===

The Midnight Hour - The Laundry Heap of my Mind

I am so on my way to sleep right now.  A scorcher today in the weather here in Toronto.  Company picnic tomorrow.  I'm one of the 3 organizers so I'll be having a wee bit of an early morning in preparation.

I learned how to boil an egg tonight.  Honestly, despite my enjoyment of experimenting in the kitchen, I've never boiled an egg before.  So tonight was a first.  Learned a trick.  Pierce the large end just through the shell.  After you're done boiling the eggs, when you go to peel and eat you'll notice the egg doesn't have that flat bottom where the pocket of air used to be.  The pierced shell lets the air and sulphur escape during the cooking process.

Wonders never cease.

I before e, except after c.  (And of course, the words that are exceptions to that rule.)

Hell, I'm just glad I learned English from birth.  There are so many exceptions to rules that are exceptions to other rules that I truly don't think I could have ever even attempted it as a second language.  And congratulations to those that can claim English as a second language they have.  I'm impressed.

I watched half of a mini-series today that was from the BBC I think, and aired on Space a few times over the past few years.  Gormenghast.  It's based on the book by the same name.  (I think).  It's amazing seeing the first half for the second time and seeing it in an entirely different light.

We all have fears.  Such wicked fears they can be.  Many we are powerless to 'overcome' and instead 'deal' with them or integrate them into our lives in some way.  I say that only because watching Gormenghast so far has made me wonder if the author shared some of the same fears as myself.

A stagnant oasis is no oasis at all.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 6/26/2005 at 12:49 AM]

=== Wednesday June 22, 2005 ===

Stream of Unconciousness

I've asked myself many questions in these past few months.
Some of which I know the answers to, some of which I still don't know
the answers to, and some of which the questions became the answers
themselves.  I don't want there to ever be a point in my life
where there are no more questions.  And by life I mean however
long our conciousness keeps ticking.  When I was growing up in my
Roman Catholic family I learned a great deal about the bible.  A
concept that I remember frightening me even at an earlier age was the
concept of heaven.  Where everyone is happy.  At peace.
I think part of it is that adult figures would always say 'All your
questions will be answered then.'.  Like the afterlife would bring
us instant enlightenment.

This concept has scared me over
the years in a kind of increasing way.  I have found happiness in
life with the fact that there are things to learn and be
discovered.  That I can plant 10 seeds and each will grow a
different way.  That feet running across sand never feels the
exact same way twice, and that even something as simple as a wheel and
axel system fascinates me.  I do not want there to ever be a point
where all my questions have been answered.  And while I realize
that I should probably be careful what I wish for, it's just how I
feel.

I'm already looking forward to
the Autumn, as I've previously mentioned numerous times.  'Tis my
favourite season of them all.  Crisp.  If I had to describe
it in one word.  And ironically, it's the time of the year I find
to be most alive.  It's spirit is strong, I think, even more so
than the spring.  It's mustering it's strength for the winter
ahead, to take it to spring.  Autumn is alive for me more than
Spring could ever be.  It's my Shangri-La, except unlike the
Actual Shangri-La I'm able to return to it year after year even after
leaving it's 3 month embrace.

I like to understand.
What i mean is, I like to know how things work.  To figure them
out.  I think it's part of my undoing.  But something I've
realized this spring is that there are some things I will not be able
to 'figure out' for certain.  And you know what?  I'm okay
with that.  I've made my peace with that.  (Yes, truly I
have, despite the fact it's a frequent topic of conversation.
Consider it positive affirmation.)

I also like that tomorrow is
the middle of the week.  And that I'll be asleep within minutes
after writing these words on this page.  Sleep.  It keeps me
coming back for more.

Peace,

Shane
[Posted 6/22/2005 at 2:28 AM]

=== Monday June 20, 2005 ===

The Power to Change

You know, I should really stop complaining about things that I have the power to change.  It's a remarkable thing really, our ability to see something we don't like in our lives and actively change something so that it doesn't exist anymore.  I never used to use this space to gripe like I seem to now.  If I'm too tired, I suppose I can go to sleep earlier.  If I can't handle stress piling up with work, I can quit or organize myself there more.  We are such agents of change.  In the end, I guess it's up to me to make it happen.

+++

It's a beautiful day today.  The sun is out, and it's not so hot as to warrant flashbacks to a couple of weeks ago.  I woke up this morning is another thing I enjoy about today.  I was dreaming something this morning and kept going back into it between snooze-button hits.  Last week I dreamt I had a family.  I married a woman who lived on the ocean and already had kids.  I fell in love and before things were set and on their full path the sky was dotted with winged invaders.  Or, rather, invaders flying in on winged creatures.  We were separated, but I swore I'd be back to get them.  I escaped with someone else that lived on the coast by diving into the water and being able to hold my breath.  It was one of those times where I was still in the dream, and felt part of it, but also knew I was only sleeping and that being under water couldn't kill me.  That I was breathing in my sleep while I dreamt, so could stay under the water in my dream with such knowledge just 'breathing' the water.  Our intention was to get information on the creatures on a nearby island.  (Long swims don't take so long when dreaming).  We were found out however, and I awoke shortly afterward.

Sure, I'd prefer my dreams not to suffer from 'starcrossed lover syndrome', however, I always enjoy the adventure.

In any case, back to work for me.  Hope your Monday is going well.

Peace,

Shane

=== Monday June 20, 2005 ===

1:00 AM on a Sunday Night

I find myself awake on this Sunday night... or Monday morning without a desire to sleep but with a need to do so.  I'm dead tired.  But the thing that keeps stoping me is that I know when I go to sleep, it'll only be hours until work.

To Work.  To work, perchance to sleep.
To sleep, an unlife in toil behind flat-screened lcd panels
while life shouts it's existence behind plate-glass windows
farther off the ground than anyone should be
when Summer grass grows strong and tall below.
Where thunder storms raise only muffled booms
and endless thinking looms and looms and looms
Where freedom lives, if not for lust of weekend nights,
Alive all hours, swarming 'neath the city lights.

But work to money then to food and rent,
A life so in-between is constant spent.

++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Bleh, me tired.  No type, me.  Ugh.  Eyes closed, I listen.

Peace,

Shane

2) It's been leaking out as quickly as I drink it down, through hundreds of thousands of what are apparently perforations in my skin.

Again I re-iterate.  I really don't mind the heat during the day, but I'd really love it if it would just suddenly be between 10 and 17 at night.  With a nice breeze so I could get some circulation in the apartment.  It's supposed to be around 22 degrees tonight. === Sunday June 5, 2005 ===

Oh where, oh were are the cool summer nights?

I'm almost certain I've complained about heat before, but here's the deal.  I'd love the summer a whole lot more if it was a constant temperature like say... 17-20 degrees Celsius.  Don't get me wrong, I'd even enjoy a hotter heat if it weren't a humid heat.  Or if it cooled down a whole lot more at night.  But that just isn't always the case next to this great lake we like to call Ontario.  I blame it on the mercury in the water.  I mean, mercury's boiling point is higher than water, so I'm pretty sure that's causing the water to near boil off in the summertime sending hundreds of thousands of gallons of evaporated hot water into the air.  This water of course causes a thick and oppressive haze over the city increasing the heat retention and humidity.

Now, that's kind of like what we may or may not expect the earth to be like down the road depending on how things go with our environmental meddling.  But I digress.

On a positive note, the haze over the city always seems to make for a psychedelic sunset.

So I long for the Autumn again.  I could stand for the whole year being Autumn I think.  Crisp nights, cool days.  Wind, wind, wind.

G'night,

Shane

=== Friday June 3, 2005 ===

Word!

I don't  know where my love of words stems from exactly.  I mean, I can't find a point where I decided they were for me.  I do remember I liked books and bookshelves.  At first, for the pictures on the pages.  Then for the pictures in my head.  When I was very young my favourite thing in the world was the childrens section of the Bramalea library.  There were stuffed animals, and a miniature house in which I remember reading through books.  Or at least, looking through the books.

Dr. Seuss was my hero.  Playing with the words, though to me it wasn't playing with words.  How was I to know at that age what were true words and what were made up rhymes placed to fit the feel of the verse.  He was my hero and still is.  The Lorax in particular is one of my favourite works of his.  I remember watching the movie on reel in the school library when I was in Kindergarten or grade one.  I'm pretty sure I cried back then, and I imagine even watching it now would strike the same nerves in me.

Regardless of how, I did fall in love with words.  How they are formed, how they can be shaped to suite one purpose or another.  Or both at the same time.

Without further ado, tonight's Scrabble board.  It marks the first time ever I've been able to place all 7 tiles at one time.  You can see it in the entry 'Dragons' just right of center.

I don't know if it'll be a hit to be posting these boards all the time, but I'm going to after each game because I think seeing how a board turns out is interesting.  A record of a moment.

(Ugh, I'm not a fan of how these pictures look these days.  Considering the actual resolution, it's a little pixely.  Hopefully just click for clearer picture.)

Peace,

Shane

=== Saturday July 30, 2005 ===

I remember, oh yes I do

This picture is a very inside joke directed directly at the one individual for whom it means anything (there is another but I do not know if they will ever see this).

Think avid card-player meets drastic misunderstanding and you may enter a place known only as the hilarity zone.  :-)

[IMAGE: http://x64.xanga.com/5ec850655723010789347/z8000650.jpg]

Sorry to anyone else who happens to check this post by me.  It has no bearing on anything at all related to anything else at all.

I wish you a peaceful Saturday evening.  I went to my first 'Karaoke' event last night at a place similar to what some of you may know as K-TV in China.  It was an interesting outing.  Two songs that I partook in were Hotel California and 'Every Morning'.  The majority of the song selections available were Chinese songs with only Chinese characters to read.  And while I'm trying to learn some Mandarin both written and spoken, I am not even close to being able to follow one of those songs.

Also, did some badminton and squash again this week.  I'm in training.  My mentor is a co-worker who has played since they were 12 and have an almost obsessive relationship with badminton.  Needless to say, I may never reach the 'obsessive' stage, but I'm definitely learning quite a bit about the game.

Many of you may hear 'badminton' and think quaint English sport that's slow paced and somewhat fun.  (Or not fun as the case may be.).  Badminton is, on the other hand, a very fast paced game involving consistent running back and forth and very fast reflexes.  It's hell on my body right now as the muscles required haven't been used since I last played tennis.  Which is quite a long time ago.

Anyway, this is somewhat of a mundane update of what's been going on.  I'm dead tired from Toronto today and I'm going to sleep now.  So I can go shopping in the morning for groceries.  And pre-haps go see a movie in the afternoon.

Today was good.  It's all getting better.  And fuckin-eh it's a beautiful life.

Peace,

Shane

=== Monday July 18, 2005 ===

Seeking

There is a movie that I have seen in parts, but not from start to end.  The movie is called Wide Awake and I believe it is an incredible movie.  Well, it was written by M. Night Shyamalan and is the story of a boy who basically goes through a year in a quest to find God while coping with the death of his Grandfather.  The topics that are covered through the eyes of such a young but most definitely precocious child are remarkable.  In his search for something specific he finds something non-specific but maybe even more profound about life.

I know why the story hits me as it does.  It hits me because of my own quest.  Because of my own seeking in life.  I recommend seeing this movie if you haven't... and if you're interested in such things.  The main character is a kid in grade school, a school run by nuns, but if you can put to the side that it's main character is years younger than you are currently yourself you'll get a great deal from this movie.  At least, I think you will.  At least, I know I did.

In other news, not much is new though I know I haven't posted in a fairly long time.  My interest is a series of waves in the ocean.  Sometimes they are peaks, and sometimes they are valleys.  Right now I'm in a valley, but that can only mean peaks are ahead.  And it's lofty peaks that I aspire to... and that only means I may have to go through some deep valleys before I get to those lofty peaks.  Such is balance, but I accept that.

So it's with that that I take my leave this evening.  I'll be around, I'm always around.  I just may be more absent than present.  Hell, I'll probably be here en-force come the next full moon.  And that's not too far away at all.

Peace,

Shane

=== Tuesday July 5, 2005 ===

The Faces We Wear

[IMAGE: http://x5c.xanga.com/1ea82152557309227602/z7088930.jpg]

I have my heart set on it.  Transcendence.  But I'm doing it up Shane-style.  My way or no way.  We're all products of infinite possibilities.  And as I used to joke around in grade 9 math, half of infinity is the same as the whole of it.  Whole of it.  Now that's funny.  So, we are all of us shining specs of infinite possibility, and the entirety of what we truly know as fact is less than an infinite fraction of an infinitely large number.

I mean, really.  How can  you say we're not all connected?  If you prick yourself, do I not bleed?  Seriously though.  Beneath the surface, haven't you pondered that thought?  The interconnectedness of those secret parts of our mind that only sometimes open themselves up to us?  In your favourite place, where the world fades and becomes clearer at the same time.  That crystal vision where you feel as if you were everything around you.

Oh, I fully realize that there will often be people who read the things I write and do the little twirl of the finger beside the ear.  But I also know that many of the people who pass their eyes along my words understand what I mean, and even sometimes entertain the ideas presented.  And it's those people I like to direct my conversations.  Open minded people.

That brings me to another topic about faces and masks.  I bring this up because, well, I don't really have to explain do I?  I bring it up because that's what came out when I started typing the title.  I just go with it, I swear I don't come up with half the stuff I write.  I probably get fed lines from that collective unconscious well.

There are very few people who do not wear masks or different faces depending on the people they are around.  I say very few because I like to entertain the possibility that there are people out there who just are who they are.  I'm not one of them, though I try and try.  I'm getting better, but let me ask you this?  Are you who you truly are, or have you put on a mask for so long that you actually have become the mask rather than the face beneath?  I only wonder because I wonder about my own masks over the years.

When I was a very young child I was fearless.  I would ask questions of anyone.  In my mind there was not a single soul that would do me harm.  There was nothing in the world I wouldn't have done on a whim if I knew it was there to do.  (I only drew the line at monkey bars.  I had a slight fear of falling from heights, though it was the hitting the ground at the end that truly always bothered me.).  So, gradually, this fearlessness grew into learning what was 'expected' of me.  As I grew and grew I became very good at doing what was expected of me in front of the people who expected it.

Oh man, this is getting into another me conversation.  And while this is indeed my weblog, I'm too tired to keep going along this thread.  I'm going to do what is maybe not expected and cut this very short.  I have a challenge for you.  For myself.  In situations where you are aware of a shift from the you face to the mask face, take off the mask.  Try the you face in front of those people who expect the mask.  The people who cringe and say "Oh. My. God.  Put that damn MASK back on." are probably not people you really want hanging around anyhow.

Just be yourself.  It's truly the least stressful state in which you can live.  And that leads to a longer life.  Which means I have more opportunity to talk with all of you.  (yes, I have a right to have a selfish reason to want people around me to live longer)

Anyhew, I. am. so. out.

I've probably already fallen asleep.  I suppose I'll have to log in tomorrow morning to verify that I didn't just type this entry in a dream and that it is part of my 'real' life.

Sweet dreams when you get there,

Shane

[Posted 7/5/2005 at 1:37 AM]

=== Monday July 4, 2005 ===

untitled and unfinished

too much time in passing, passes
deep within that void we make of life
between a smile and a tear
we hit our heads on walls, and wonder
why it hurts along the way to where
happiness once bloomed and thrived

to where we knew the comfort of arms
the solace of legs, and the saftey of hands

+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

I'm heading to bed now.  It's late, but the thing about late nights such as these is the creativity that always seems to find me when I should be sleeping.  I think that the 'untitled and unfinished' is the title of the work above.  Sometimes we get so locked into our circular ruts we forget we're not tied to the millwheel.  We re-create each day for ourselves over and over never completing them as we would.  Untitled and unfinished.

Find me.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 7/4/2005 at 1:58 AM]

=== Tuesday August 30, 2005 ===

Shane the Last-Minute Wonder
There's no stress like no stress.

Well, I'm a bit of a procrastinator.  The 'type a\type b' thing is a bit limited, but I'd say I'm well in to the depths of being a Type B personality.  You'd think leaving things to the last minute gets stressful... but I find if I let things happen they work out in the end.  Take one find weekend I went to my Grandparents 50th anniversary.  I think it was the 50th.  Regardless, I found myself without a suit as my job was business casual.  In fact, I own an almost exclusively business casual wardrobe much to my chagrin.  I'm probably in serious need of fashion salvation, but that's really another story.

The point is, it's the evening before I head out on a 5 hour journey to Sudbury and I am still in dire need of a suit.  "Don't worry" my inner voice says, we'll just pick one up at Moore's downtown.  I'm on a limited budget, on a very limited timeframe, and need a suit.  I walk into the shop and start looking around.  The prices all seem above my budget at the time would allow.  I find four suits in the entire shop that are within my range.  And you know what?  One of the four fit perfectly off the rack.  No adjustments necessary.

Needless to say I pick up my passport tomorrow.  I fly out to Nevada on Wednesday from Buffalo.

Pager on the other hand was hell this weekend.  Sleepless nights and sleepless days.  I'm going to sleep VERY well on the plane.  You can bet on that.

Peace, and good night,

(I hope),

Shane

[Posted 8/30/2005 at 1:21 AM]

=== Friday August 26, 2005 ===

Chai Tea and Pager Nights
Another Chapter in Pager/Shane Relations

It begins not with a page but with a promise of many of our customers wanting someone (an anonymous pager person we shall name ME for the sake of representation) to monitor their servers this weekend.  It further began with only monitoring of certain processes that run only between the hours of 9pm - 2am.  And it was good.  Or at the very least, it was acceptable.  It continued later with monitoring of processes that run during the day on Saturday and Sunday between the hours of 10am and 6pm.  And it was less than good.  But workable.  Add to the mix a last minute phonecall from someone in my office asking me to monitor yet a different process altogether tomorrow morning at 7am and I break out my Chai tea and honey.

I'd run across the street for an imported Red Bull from Poland but despite any actual evidence yet to the contrary I fear what those damned things are actually doing to me when I have them.  I have visions of my life ending 20 years before it's natural termination due to whatever is in those energy drinks 'speeding up' my days when I use them.  Thus burning me out twice as fast.

Moving on though, to my apparently non-stop monitoring, we find an exhausted Shane wondering about how he'll deal with an actual page amidst all this active monitoring.  We also find an exhausted Shane contemplating further along his next career choice.  And chuckling at the future that waits.  My current job is in tech-support for software my company creates.  My next career move is going to be one that lets me do what I am passionate about.  Lets me work with writing, and with people, and with psychology as well.  More to come on that front.

So I'm drinking Chai tea with honey, twitching when the T.V. has a cell phone go off in a show.

But life.  I like it.  I can't really complain about anything.  You're all swell.

Oh, and next Wednesday is closer than ever.  I can almost taste the desert air.  The only thing stopping me is that I've never tasted the desert air before.

Peace, I may be around again this weekend.  Being chained to my desk chair as I am.

Shane

[Posted 8/26/2005 at 11:27 PM]

=== Thursday August 25, 2005 ===

I've Got Five Minutes

I've got five minutes and I think I'm going to rable.  Things are well with me, and getting better as well.  There's a path opening up for me, or rather, I'm beating one down.  I'll be the captain of my own ship soon.  By soon I mean within a year I hope.  If all goes well.  There is a demand out there, and I'm thinking of a way to supply that demand while doing what I enjoy and making money at the same time.

No silly, I'm not talking about prostitution.  That life is long ago, and so far behind me now.

So I'm excited, but that's all I'm going to say because I always blab and spill the beans before they're cooked.  And damnit, I deserve to have some cooked beans for once.

On the flip side, I'm on pager tomorrow.  Then, the day I hand over pager next wednesday, I'm headed to Nevada for some burning man action.  Whatever that means.  As I've said countless times, I have no idea what I'm in for.  But I'm looking forward to some adventure on the high dessert seas.  I'm hoping for what I understand can be pretty spectacular storms that sweep in and sweep out quickly, but marvelously.  Because a storm in the middle of the dessert, that would be very positively portentious for me.

I'm going to go to sleep now for what I hope is my fourth night in a row of 8 hours sleep in a row.  I'm spoiling myself only because I know that come tomorrow I"ll be getting very scattered sleep.  I deserve to feel comfortable at least tonight.

Peace,

Shane

=== Sunday August 14, 2005 ===

The Bruno

The Bruno got married today.  The Bruno is the phenomenon that is also my mother's brother... which makes him my uncle.  He's the youngest of my mother's siblings, and has been a bachelor since the day I was born.  On this day in future history, he became wed to a woman named Jen.  In a ceremony marked with love, a reception marked with humour and tears, and a hopping dance floor, an era was brought to an end.  The Bruno.  Is.  Married.

He's in love deep, and as some of you may know, I love seeing that in people.  I definately miss feeling that too.  But that's besides the point really.  The speaches were so touching the DJ was in tears, and everyone knew exactly what a momentus occasion this indeed was.  I'd have pictures for you tonight, but my camera always runs out of batteries at the most inoportune times.  (At least, the times I remember to even bring it.  I'd forget about yesterday if today's dawn wasn't a constant reminder that there ever was a yesterday.)

I've also discovered something.  If I'm going to drink alcohol, I have to go all the way, or none at all.  Alcohol is a depressant.  But I don't feel it when I'm drinking and maintaining a buzz all night.  But tonight I stopped for some reason, at some point, and became somewhat melancholy.  It was at that point I felt very out of place and the joy worked against me.

But in retrospect, it was a great evening.  I guess it just leads me to a confession.  You know how I love people who are unabashedly themselves?  It's because I find it hard to be that.  I definately need to pair myself with someone outgoing.  Otherwise I shudder to think how the children of two incredibly shy people would turn out... however, that leads me to another thought.  I'm not shy around friends that know me well.  More and more I revert to shy around the family who remember who I've always been.  It's like I'm trying to stay within the cookie cut-out they know me as.  I'm going to burningman for the love of god.  I'm not this incredibly shy person any more.  Truly.  Sometimes I'm somewhat shy, but as I said, for people who have known me before, even close friends, I always revert to uber-shy moody guy.

Anyway, I'm off to bed to recover, it was a good night.

And thanks for all of your comments over the last little while.  I have some catching up to do tomorrow with all of your sites.  In the last two weeks I think I've only been home for two nights.  Crazy times.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 8/14/2005 at 2:11 AM]

=== Monday August 8, 2005 ===

[IMAGE: http://x08.xanga.com/00914021394a41406094/z1358105.jpg]Memories - Snapshots of the Universe

I haven't spoken to you since we locked eyes and our only words were in our mind.  The problem is most people forget, and then slowly remember until they sit in silence facing the window at the autumn of their lives and everything is as clear to them as this moment.

Confusion of the present is the clarity of the past.  We walk with giants, every one of us stands tall.

I'm going back to work tomorrow.  I don't know what tomorrow will bring.  There was a time I thought it would bring exactly what I was looking for, but the fatal flaw with that thinking is that I never figured out what it was I was looking for.  So tomorrow came, and it came again, and for all my waiting the sun never rose with perfect colours.  I never asked for tomorrow to be anything solid.  So tomorrow never answered my unasked questions.

The question I really have.  It's in there twittering.  The question I have is 'Will I ever be finished?'.  If I decide to take a step forward.  To pick a direction and walk it with such fierceness that any wall I approach will shy away from my path... if I do walk that way, will I ever be happy with the path?

I feel so silly.  I'm 25 years old.  But I'm pretty sure no matter where I go, in 10 years, in 20... I'll feel exactly the same as I do now about the fundamentals.  The same questions, and the same smile.

I'm unsettled.  Mostly, right now I think I'm unsettled because I'm so busy with work as well as personal life.  Between working on my squash and badminton game, trying to get my passport hammered down, getting a suit for this coming weekend, and working at the place I work... i don't know where I get to breathe.  And hell yeah I know compared to some I have it easy.  This isn't a question of me 'complaining' for the sake of.  All I'm saying is if this is how it keeps going on I'm going to be 80 before I know it, and for the love of God please stick me on a mountain top somewhere now so I don't miss it all as it passes by.

I don't want to miss a single flower on the side of the road.  Not a single rose.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 8/8/2005 at 1:14 AM]

=== Thursday August 4, 2005 ===

unstoppable balls meet unbreakable walls

I can't stop writing words tonight,
they writhe inside my mind
like worms on pavement after summer rain.

Seeking shelter before the sun reveals
relentlessy baking them where they squirm.

I dare not challenge sol to stop me now
for fear of as competitive a soul as myself

but age old questions could be answered
if it were so

+++

shane d. fera

=== Thursday August 4, 2005 ===

Flor De Llaneza

i remember old and wrinkled
kind, and pipe smoke wafted
knee-bent in the grass behind
the picnic table by the lake

he, kindred i, our eyes meet
teacher, great grandfather
patience and love

and pipe-smoke wafted
dream-filled summer days

+++

shane d. fera

=== Wednesday August 3, 2005 ===

time. and again

you smell of eternity
which is why the wind
caresses your face
to turn towards yesterday
if only for a while

you don't belong in this moment
but you remember when
and then, and what once was
as clearly as you remember
what the sky looked like
as you see it now

i smell of awe
which is why the wind
cannot touch my face
for all my longing in trees
and fields of long grass

i cannot see yesterday as now
for I belong in this moment
what is and is and is
while I remember right now
eternally this present
and crystal place

but you and I will meet
where wind touches crystal
perfection in a time where time
cannot exist in thought
where we destroy each other
and create ourselves again

+++

shane d. fera

(I am tired and this moment is kicking me to my too-warm matress and single sheet where I lay in perpetual yearning for the perfect time of year where no complaint will ever touch my lips.  The fiery and passionate Autumn where winding down is static electricity in the air, and the smells are far more alive than sluggish pedestrians burning in the midday sun.)

=== Sunday September 25, 2005 ===

Time for a Change

Well folks, this isn't a 'goodbye' post by any means.  I'm continuing my posting at a new site that I'll reference later.  The fact is I have many people here that I consider friend.  I'll always keep reading and commenting, but I just won't be showing up in your SIR lists with any new posts.  My new home is ShaneFera.com and I've begun slowly moving many of my older posts from archives over to be in the archives over there.  I know that my leaving Xanga means that many of the people who read my posts will not get any 'updates' as per Xanga's usual dish.  I'm not sure how many of you will be over to read from time to time at my new site, but I'll be kicking around here commenting as usual.

It's been almost 6 years since I first got my Ego stroked by a mysterious woman *cough*marketing machination*cough* named Bianca.

That being said, it's time for a change.

Peace to you all,
and ever much love,

Shane Fera (aka. Abaxial, Stultiloquent, and Akatiez)

=== Wednesday September 7, 2005 ===

Two Lost Canadians
(A Burning Man Adventure)
by Shane Fera

)'(

I have some time today, and some energy, to relate to you some of my experiences at Burning Man in Nevada.  Since I only remember things after I live them, now is the perfect time for me to share.

A friend of mine and I decided this year to dive into the Burning Man experience.  It began with something that went like this:

"Blah blah blah... burningman.  Blah blah." My friend said.
"Really?"  I asked? "You know, I heard about that about 4 years ago and have wanted to go since."
"Yeah?  You wanna go this year?" He said, most likely half-jokingly.
"Hell yeah!" I stated, knowing this year's theme was psyche.  "This year's theme is practically calling to me."
"You do?  Well lets do it!"

Thus began the saga.  Upon landing in Reno we needed some sleep, as it was early in the morning and the prospect of driving through unknown territory in the middle of the Nevada desert just didn't appeal to either of us.  The next morning we headed over to Costco and Wal-Mart for our supplies.  As it happens, it seems most 'Burn' participants had the same idea and we saw a consistent flow of people with carts stocked with gallons of water, energy bars, and Gatorade.  Our anticipation rose.  Upon reaching Home Hardware and seeing a sign 'Burning Man Supplies' pasted to the entrance, we knew we were almost there.  And truthfully, the adventure really began as we shoved off from Reno onto the I-80 across towards the Black Rock Desert.

The road to the campsite consisted of a line of RV's, trucks, and in some cases higher-end cars all headed to the same place.  As we approached the gate, we were greeted by someone looking for our tickets, and spotting us as burn-virgins instantly as we were dressed as any Canadian first-timers might be dressed.  In khaki shorts and a golf shirt.  With a fishing hat to keep the hot sun out of our eyes.  His words "Welcome Home" resonated with us, and sparked the true dawn of the weekend.

We drove into the camping area, where 25 thousand other campers were scattered on the actually very organized and delineated streets.  Our first attempt to set up camp was met with rejection.  We pulled into an empty space near a sign that stated "Anonymous Camp".  I thought; cool, that's fitting.  We don't know anyone here, we're two anonymous Canadians. Little did we know what was to come.  As we emptied the back of the Explorer and began to set up the tent we were approached by a nearby camper who asked, "Are you two with Anonymous Camp?".  Of course we weren't and stated as such.  That's about the time she mentions the fact that they're expecting a few RV's and that it's an Alcoholics Anonymous camp... as I glance over the cases of beer poking out from under our luggage.  Embarrassed slightly, but no less energetic about getting set up and on our way, we made our way back out into the camp roads in search of another site.

We settled on a gap located near the junction of streets called 'Gestalt' and 6 o-clock.  This time as we set up camp we were greeted by whom I can only guess was a veteran of the event offering us Burning Man cookies.  I took some and enjoyed my first taste of what Burning Man is all about.  I was going to jokingly comment about how after eating the cookies is when everything went fuzzy but the cookies were not laced with anything 'interesting' and were in fact just some good shortbread cookies covered with icing in the shape of the Man.

The Man as I call him... as everyone calls him, is the object of the event standing in the center of the grounds raised up on a platform and covered on neon lights for the evenings.  Underneath him this year is a funhouse maze of 44 odd rooms through which you have to traverse to get to the second and third floors.  As we walked out onto the 'Playa' on that first night (which is the empty desert between the camps and the man) we were in awe of everything.  Sensory overload is the only way to describe what all the drifting music and lights from all directions created in us.  Grinning from ear to ear we knew this was it.  Absolutely more than we both had expected.  Exponentially more.  And the phrase 'Fuckin' Eh' was constantly on my lips for the remainder of the weekend.

To describe what it was like is difficult.  It truly is something you have to experience.  We tried to relate it to something we could explain to people that might make them understand. The 'Mad Max' movie on Acid was one such attempt.  Perhaps with a smattering of every holiday rolled into one as well.  The vastness of the 'Playa' is hard to describe as well... needless to say I did more walking in the past week than I did in the last year.  I'm almost certain of that.  There were pieces of art and 'Mutant Cars' all over the Playa.  Flashing their lights and emitting their music everywhere.  Camps set up to draw people in, camps set up with 'Keep Out' signs as well.

Something for everyone is what it is.  Freedom of expression at it's finest... freedom period.  And not an ounce of anything but the purest of goodwill from everyone there is what I mostly sensed.  A giant face hoisted up in the air with projection of a speaking face projected onto it stated on our first night. "Whatever you think Burning Man is, it's not.  Enjoy your Burn."  For the first time, I'm at a loss for words to truly describe everything I saw or heard.  Not to mention I need to get back to work from lunch in about 5 minutes.  I have some video footage that I hope to have available for download from my website for you all.  At least until my bandwidth limit is exceeded.  Even the panoramic shots where I attempt to relay the vastness and size of the event doesn't do it justice.

All I can say is, if you like art, if you like music, if you like to dance, if you like to sit in the sun, if you like to camp, or if you like to meet people, or if you like to be surrounded by people being freely themselves, I highly recommend this event.  And if you do plan to go next year let me know.  I plan to go also.  The impression I got, and what I'd like to do this year, is form a camp as other people form camps.  Just groups of people who have something in common, or nothing in common, and they reserve a section of space in the camp.

Back to the grind for me now, but I'll be back again eventually.  I actually have some semblance of energy today.  And am feeling much better about my situation at work.  Life is in perspective just a little bit more.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 9/7/2005 at 2:55 PM]

=== Saturday October 22, 2005 ===

Tabula Rasa

This moment I am.
Despite what reason dictates,
smoke and mirrors do not
cage my present.

Though I cannot, beyond
a shadow of a doubt,
exclaim my momentous living breath
with the dedication of a martyr
or the constancy of a saint;
I believe that I exist.

Therefore,
right now,
I do.

+++

[Posted 10/22/2005 at 1:52 AM]

=== Wednesday October 19, 2005 ===

Punmaster General

Well, I can't believe what I just realized about a classic game I used to enjoy as a very young child.

For those of you who know of the game 'Frogger' it's about a frog trying to cross a highway and then a river.

If you make it to the other side you have to land on one of five or six openings.  On these openeings can appear a wolf or a fly.

If you get the wolf you die.  But if you land on a fly, your time refills.

What I just got, after years of not realizing it (because I hadn't noticed the 'time' bar before.):

Time Flies!  Ha!

Anyway, I thought it was hillarious.

There goes my youth.

Peace,

Shane

=== Tuesday October 18, 2005 ===

eyes

I fell into her eyes first,
foot over head
(where I thought darkness never tread)
a blinding bliss of wrapping arms
and never ever tomorrows

her eyes were not for me to stay
upon those oceans
(depths delved while speaking deviotions)
tangled hearts, and heartless words
chasing after tomorrows

lidded now, and facing west
she speaks no more
(not words, nor flickers, a silent roar)
reaching minds remembering each other
seeking past tomorrows

+++

=== Tuesday October 18, 2005 ===

Magnetic Poetry

With words we only know what reason states,
but they cannot convey what's in the soul.
Among all of those words the heart creates,
There's one from which all thought of you does roll.

Not 'silence', though your gazing eyes give pause,
Nor is it 'laughter' though your smile is bold;
And neither is it 'luminous' that draws,
Though all these words together make the mold.

You gave the word to me, wrapped in your arms,
from plastic box, a gift from me to you.
A single word, to capture that night's charms,
And yours as well, my dear, I tell you true.

Now 'Passion' sticks upon my freezer door;
A word between we two, forever more.

+++

Shane D. Fera
[Posted 10/18/2005 at 2:6 AM]

=== Saturday November 19, 2005 ===

Dread Nights and Coffee Shops

There's a 24 hour Coffee shop just at the end of my street. Lucky me. You know, until about two years ago I never drank coffee. It started at the office. A cappucino led to a coffee. A coffee led to tripple shot coffees and espressos. The fact that they keep waffling on whether or not coffee is good or bad for you gives me some comfort. If they say it's bad for you half the time, and good for you the other half, I have at least a little hope that it has no bearing on the length of my lifespan in the least. I'll just keep eating my greens and see where that takes me.

I still have a bad feeling about this weekend and pager, only because so far it has been pretty good. I now feel that if I stop having a bad feeling about this weekend that I'll suddenly find myself in the murk and mire of too many pages and too little time in which to work on them. In the meantime I'm watching 'The Shield' on DVD. The first season. Just finished the pilot episode. Looks pretty interesting so far. It's the upside of being chained to the house while on pager. At least there are things to do.

I'll probably be back with far more interesting things to say without further using the actual word itself.

[Posted 11/19/2005 at 12:57 PM]

=== Tuesday November 15, 2005 ===

Monday's always make me think of silly things like time off, or getting the hell away from where I work.  Oh, I know this weblog is attached to my name, and that if anyone at my current place of employment was 'googling' people from the office it might not be taken very well.  The fact is, where I work used to be a great place.  Truly.  Though the job is apparently the antithesis of what someone with my personality type should be working at, I still get through.  Lately, however, it's taken a turn for the worse.  Morale is reaching record lows while the number of people leaving is reaching record highs.  On the flip side, stress for me is down because I'm growing numb to the whole thing.  I don't think that's necessarily a good thing though.

I've been reading a book about visionary companies and their impact on the world by following their core values no matter what.  No such values exist where I work, or if they do they keep changing or remain unclearly stated.  I guess I'll ride the waves while I can, keep getting better at surfing, and see what plutonian shores I end up on.  Life is a ride folks, and I enjoy the ups and downs as much as I can.

Speaking of ups.  This past Friday I went to check out a band called Factor Fiction.  Great music, great lyrics, great energy.  I reccomend checking their website out, and if you live anywhere close to the area, coming out to whenever they put on their next show.  Details can be found at their website.

Anyway, I really should get my head to it's pillow for the night.  Tuesday is already here, and I haven't left Monday yet.

Peace,

Shane

[Posted 11/15/2005 at 12:58 AM]

=== Wednesday November 9, 2005 ===

Conviction

the depths of my conviction
far exceed the depths of my anger
at everything I cannot change
nor all that we will not do
before my last breath passes through
my broken lips, a whisper

yet you question that which would not falter
despite the darker nights and longer sleeps
a question that in the very asking
destroys what we have built between us

so I ask this, and expect no answer
to the back of my head

Is it done?  Are YOU done?

rhetorical; my footsteps will fade from your ears

of that I have conviction

Shane D. Fera

(Needs work :-p yes, I know.  But these things, these posts here are my first steps.  Rework.  Rework.  Rework.)

[Posted 11/9/2005 at 10:16 PM]
